Al-Sam'ani's Critique of the Mu'tazila Definition of Knowledge
Al-Sam'ani's critique of the Mu'tazila definition of knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a logical flaw in a definition by testing its comprehensiveness, using the example of God's knowledge.

Core Idea
A definition must include all instances; excluding divine knowledge invalidates the Mu'tazila definition.

This lesson examines a classic critique from al-Sam'ani against the Mu'tazila definition of knowledge. You will learn how a logical condition—comprehensiveness—is applied to a theological definition, and why even a definition that seems plausible can fail if it misses a primary case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and proposed definition
Locate the term being defined (العلم, knowledge) and the Mu'tazila definition: 'belief of a thing as it is' (اعتقاد الشيء على ما هو به).
The definiendum is universal knowledge, including divine and human knowledge.
2
Extract the logical condition being violated
Al-Sam'ani invokes the condition that a definition must be comprehensive (جامع). If it fails to include any instance of the definiendum, it is invalid.
Comprehensiveness is a standard requirement in mantiq and usul.
3
Understand why 'belief' excludes God
The term 'belief' (اعتقاد) implies acquisition and changeability, which are not applicable to God. Therefore, the definition cannot cover God's knowledge, which is a necessary instance.
This is both a semantic and theological argument.
4
Conclude the definition's invalidity
Since the definition excludes a primary instance (God), it is not comprehensive and thus not a valid definition.
Al-Sam'ani's critique is logically sound: a definition that fails the comprehensiveness condition is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ذلك أيضًا ما انتقد به السمعاني تعريف المعتزلة للعلم : مع والذي قاله بعضهم - ويعني بهم المعتزلة - : إنه (أي العلم) اعتقاد الشيء على ما هو به باطل؛ لأن الله تعالى عالم بعلم على ما نطق الكتاب والسنة، ولا يطلق عليه الاعتقاد بحال، بل هو من صفات المخلوقين. وإذا لم يكن الحد جامعا، لم يكن صحيحا.
And from that also is what al-Sam'ani criticized the Mu'tazila's definition of knowledge: and what some of them said - meaning the Mu'tazila - that it (i.e., knowledge) is a belief of a thing as it is, is false; because God Almighty is knowing with knowledge as stated in the Book and the Sunnah, and the term 'belief' is never applied to Him, rather it is among the attributes of creatures. And if the definition is not comprehensive, it is not valid.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage presents a concise critique by al-Sam'ani of the Mu'tazila definition of knowledge (al-ilm). The Mu'tazila defined knowledge as 'belief of a thing as it is' (i'tiqad al-shay' 'ala ma huwa bihi). Al-Sam'ani argues that this definition is false because it fails to be comprehensive (jami'). The term 'belief' (i'tiqad) cannot be applied to God, who is described as knowing with knowledge in the Quran and Sunnah. Since God's knowledge is not a belief (as belief implies acquisition and changeability), the definition excludes God's knowledge, which is a primary instance of knowledge. Therefore, the definition is not comprehensive and thus invalid. This critique highlights the condition that a definition must include all instances (jami'), and demonstrates how theological considerations can affect logical definitions.

Key Terms

الاعتقاد
الحد الجامع

Key Takeaway
A definition must be comprehensive; excluding any instance—especially God—renders it invalid.

Condition of Clarity in Definitions
Author explains the condition of clarity with a quote from al-Tufi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a definition is unclear due to obscurity, metaphor, or strange words, using the criteria from al-Tufi.

Core Idea
A definition must be clearer than the term it defines.

Definitions aim to clarify, so the words used must be clear. Otherwise, they add obscurity. Al-Tufi warns against ambiguous words, metaphors, and strange terms. In this lesson, you learn to evaluate a definition's clarity.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the purpose of definition
The author states that the function of definition is clarification (البيان). If the definition is unclear, it fails its purpose.
2
Identify sources of obscurity
Al-Tufi lists three: ambiguous word (mujmal), metaphor (majaz) especially if not clear, and strange word (gharib).
3
Apply the condition of relative clarity
The definition must be more evident (أجلى) than the term being defined. If it is equally hidden or more hidden, the addressee gains nothing.
4
Evaluate an example
Consider defining 'riba' using a metaphorical phrase. Check if that metaphor is clear. If not, the definition is invalid.
Use a fiqh example.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اجتناب الغموض ومظنته فيه : مهمة الحد أو التعريف هي الإيضاح والبيان، فنحن نعرف مصطلحا ما أو عبارة لكي نكشف عن معناها ونوضح المراد منها . وهذا يقتضي بداهة أن تكون العبارات المستعملة في التعريف عبارات واضحة لا لبس فيها ولا غموض، وإلا كانت سببًا في زيادة الإبهام والخفاء بدلا من أن تكون سببًا في البيان والتوضيح . يقول الطوفي : الحدود يجب أن يجتنب فيها الإبهام ومظنته كاللفظ المجمل والمجاز والغريب، خصوصا إذا لم يكن المجاز واضحا» فمن شرط الحد – إذا – أن يكون أجلى وأوضح من المفرد التصوري الذي نشرحه، فإذا كان قولنا الشارح (تعريفنا) أخفى من المفرد الذي نشرحه أو مماثلاً الخفاء، فإن المخاطب لن يستفيد شيئا من شرحنا وتعريفنا، بل يبقى في جهالته ، ولا يستطيع أن يتصور هذا المفرد الذي نشرحه له عن طريق قولنا . يقول ابن النجار الفتوحي رحمه الله : يجب مساواة الحد للمحدود، لأنه إن كان أعم فلا دلالة له على الأخص ولا يفيد التمييز، وإن كان أخص فلأنه أخفى، لأنه أقل وجودًا منه، ويجب أيضًا أن لا يكون في لفظه مجاز ولا مشترك، لأن الحد مميز للمحدود، ولا يحصل الميز مع واحد منهما» وما ذلك إلا لأن الاشتراك مخل بفهم المعنى المقصود، كما أن الغالب تبادر المعاني الحقيقية إلى الفهم دون المجازية ج - ألا يتوقف فهم التعريف على معرفة سابقة بالمعرف: ينبغي في التعريف أن نستعمل ألفاظا جديدة مباينة للفظ الذي نريد حده أو
Avoiding obscurity and its potential in it: The function of the definition (hadd) or description is clarification and explanation. We define a term or phrase to reveal its meaning and clarify what is intended. This necessarily requires that the expressions used in the definition be clear expressions with no ambiguity or obscurity; otherwise they would be a cause of increased vagueness and concealment instead of being a cause of clarification and explanation. Al-Tufi said: 'Definitions must avoid obscurity and its potential, such as the ambiguous word (mujmal), metaphor (majaz), and strange word (gharib), especially if the metaphor is not clear.' So a condition of the definition is that it be more evident and clearer than the conceptual singular we are explaining. If our explanation (our definition) is more hidden than the singular we are explaining or equal in hiddenness, then the addressee will not benefit from our explanation and definition, but rather remains in his ignorance, and cannot conceive that singular we are explaining through our speech. Ibn al-Najjar al-Futuhi (may God have mercy on him) said: 'The definition must be equal to the definiendum, because if it is more general, it does not indicate the more specific and does not benefit distinction, and if it is more specific, then it is more hidden because it is less existent than it. And it is also necessary that there be no metaphor (majaz) or homonymy (mushtarak) in its wording, because the definition distinguishes the definiendum, and distinction is not achieved with either of them.' And that is only because homonymy disrupts understanding of the intended meaning, just as usually the literal meanings come to mind before metaphorical ones. C - The understanding of the definition should not depend on prior knowledge of the definiendum: It is necessary in the definition to use new expressions different from the word we want to define or...
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage enumerates conditions for a valid definition (hadd). It begins by stating the purpose of definition: clarification and explanation. Therefore, the expressions used must be clear and free from ambiguity. The author quotes al-Tufi, who says definitions must avoid obscurity (ibham) and its potential causes: ambiguous words (mujmal), metaphor (majaz), and strange words (gharib), especially if the metaphor is unclear. Consequently, the definition must be more evident (ajla) and clearer than the conceptual singular being explained. If it is equal or more hidden, the addressee gains nothing. Next, a quote from Ibn al-Najjar al-Futuhi adds another condition: the definition must be equal (musawi) in scope to the definiendum. If it is more general (a'am), it fails to distinguish the specific; if more specific (akhass), it is more hidden because it applies to fewer things. Additionally, the wording must avoid metaphor and homonymy (ishtirak) because the definition's role is to distinguish, and these hinder distinction. Homonymy disrupts understanding, and literal meanings usually take precedence over metaphorical. Finally, the passage introduces a third condition (marked as 'j'): the definition should not require prior knowledge of the definiendum; it should use new expressions different from the term being defined. The text cuts off here. These conditions are foundational in the science of definition.

المجاز
الغريب
المجمل

Condition of Equality and Avoidance of Ambiguity in Definitions
Author presents conditions from Ibn al-Najjar on equality and avoidance of ambiguity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to check whether a definition is equal in scope to the definiendum and free from homonymy and unclear metaphor, using the criteria from Ibn al-Najjar.

Core Idea
A definition must cover exactly the definiendum and avoid words that cause confusion.

Ibn al-Najjar adds two conditions: first, the definition must be equal (musawi) to the definiendum in scope; second, its wording must avoid metaphor (majaz) and homonymy (ishtirak) because these hinder distinction. This lesson shows you how to apply these checks.

Guided Path
1
Check equality of scope
Ibn al-Najjar says if the definition is broader (a'am), it doesn't distinguish the specific; if narrower (akhass), it is more hidden. So the definition must be exactly coextensive.
2
Check absence of homonymy
A word with multiple meanings (mushtarak) confuses the intended meaning. Thus, definitions should avoid homonymous terms.
3
Check absence of unclear metaphor
Metaphor (majaz) can lead to misunderstanding because literal meanings tend to come to mind first. Only clear metaphors are acceptable, but preferably avoided.
4
Apply to a fiqh example
Take the definition of 'salah' as 'specific words and actions beginning with takbir and ending with taslim.' Does it suffer from homonymy or metaphor? Check.
Consider if 'taslim' might be ambiguous.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اجتناب الغموض ومظنته فيه : مهمة الحد أو التعريف هي الإيضاح والبيان، فنحن نعرف مصطلحا ما أو عبارة لكي نكشف عن معناها ونوضح المراد منها . وهذا يقتضي بداهة أن تكون العبارات المستعملة في التعريف عبارات واضحة لا لبس فيها ولا غموض، وإلا كانت سببًا في زيادة الإبهام والخفاء بدلا من أن تكون سببًا في البيان والتوضيح . يقول الطوفي : الحدود يجب أن يجتنب فيها الإبهام ومظنته كاللفظ المجمل والمجاز والغريب، خصوصا إذا لم يكن المجاز واضحا» فمن شرط الحد – إذا – أن يكون أجلى وأوضح من المفرد التصوري الذي نشرحه، فإذا كان قولنا الشارح (تعريفنا) أخفى من المفرد الذي نشرحه أو مماثلاً الخفاء، فإن المخاطب لن يستفيد شيئا من شرحنا وتعريفنا، بل يبقى في جهالته ، ولا يستطيع أن يتصور هذا المفرد الذي نشرحه له عن طريق قولنا . يقول ابن النجار الفتوحي رحمه الله : يجب مساواة الحد للمحدود، لأنه إن كان أعم فلا دلالة له على الأخص ولا يفيد التمييز، وإن كان أخص فلأنه أخفى، لأنه أقل وجودًا منه، ويجب أيضًا أن لا يكون في لفظه مجاز ولا مشترك، لأن الحد مميز للمحدود، ولا يحصل الميز مع واحد منهما» وما ذلك إلا لأن الاشتراك مخل بفهم المعنى المقصود، كما أن الغالب تبادر المعاني الحقيقية إلى الفهم دون المجازية ج - ألا يتوقف فهم التعريف على معرفة سابقة بالمعرف: ينبغي في التعريف أن نستعمل ألفاظا جديدة مباينة للفظ الذي نريد حده أو
Avoiding obscurity and its potential in it: The function of the definition (hadd) or description is clarification and explanation. We define a term or phrase to reveal its meaning and clarify what is intended. This necessarily requires that the expressions used in the definition be clear expressions with no ambiguity or obscurity; otherwise they would be a cause of increased vagueness and concealment instead of being a cause of clarification and explanation. Al-Tufi said: 'Definitions must avoid obscurity and its potential, such as the ambiguous word (mujmal), metaphor (majaz), and strange word (gharib), especially if the metaphor is not clear.' So a condition of the definition is that it be more evident and clearer than the conceptual singular we are explaining. If our explanation (our definition) is more hidden than the singular we are explaining or equal in hiddenness, then the addressee will not benefit from our explanation and definition, but rather remains in his ignorance, and cannot conceive that singular we are explaining through our speech. Ibn al-Najjar al-Futuhi (may God have mercy on him) said: 'The definition must be equal to the definiendum, because if it is more general, it does not indicate the more specific and does not benefit distinction, and if it is more specific, then it is more hidden because it is less existent than it. And it is also necessary that there be no metaphor (majaz) or homonymy (mushtarak) in its wording, because the definition distinguishes the definiendum, and distinction is not achieved with either of them.' And that is only because homonymy disrupts understanding of the intended meaning, just as usually the literal meanings come to mind before metaphorical ones. C - The understanding of the definition should not depend on prior knowledge of the definiendum: It is necessary in the definition to use new expressions different from the word we want to define or...
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage enumerates conditions for a valid definition (hadd). It begins by stating the purpose of definition: clarification and explanation. Therefore, the expressions used must be clear and free from ambiguity. The author quotes al-Tufi, who says definitions must avoid obscurity (ibham) and its potential causes: ambiguous words (mujmal), metaphor (majaz), and strange words (gharib), especially if the metaphor is unclear. Consequently, the definition must be more evident (ajla) and clearer than the conceptual singular being explained. If it is equal or more hidden, the addressee gains nothing. Next, a quote from Ibn al-Najjar al-Futuhi adds another condition: the definition must be equal (musawi) in scope to the definiendum. If it is more general (a'am), it fails to distinguish the specific; if more specific (akhass), it is more hidden because it applies to fewer things. Additionally, the wording must avoid metaphor and homonymy (ishtirak) because the definition's role is to distinguish, and these hinder distinction. Homonymy disrupts understanding, and literal meanings usually take precedence over metaphorical. Finally, the passage introduces a third condition (marked as 'j'): the definition should not require prior knowledge of the definiendum; it should use new expressions different from the term being defined. The text cuts off here. These conditions are foundational in the science of definition.

Conditions for a Valid Definition (Hadd)
Author lists conditions for definition: clarity, avoiding ambiguity, metaphor, homonymy, and circularity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify violations of the five conditions for a valid definition: clarity, coextensiveness, avoidance of metaphor, homonymy, and circularity.

Core Idea
A valid definition must be clearer, coextensive, literal, and non-circular.

Defining a term is the first step in any disciplined inquiry. But how do you know if a definition is actually doing its job? The classical logicians and jurists laid out precise conditions. This passage from Jadal Usuliyyin presents the key criteria that transform a mere string of words into a genuine explanation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of definition
The author states that the purpose of definition (hadd) is clarification and explanation. Keep this goal in mind as you examine each condition.
2
Apply the clarity condition
Check that the definition uses clear, unambiguous expressions. If the definition is as obscure as or more obscure than the term being defined, it fails. Avoid ambiguous words (mujmal), metaphor (majaz), and strange terms (gharib).
Al-Tufi emphasizes avoiding these pitfalls.
3
Check coextensiveness
The definition must be exactly equivalent to the defined (musawi). If it is broader (a'amm) or narrower (akhass), it does not correctly distinguish the defined from other things.
Ibn al-Najjar al-Futuhi's condition.
4
Exclude metaphor and homonymy
Metaphor (majaz) and homonymy (ishtirak) must not appear in the wording, because they prevent the definition from uniquely identifying the defined.
The author explains that homonymy impairs understanding, and literal meanings dominate.
5
Detect circularity
Ensure that understanding the definition does not require prior knowledge of the defined term. If it does, circularity (dawr) occurs, which is rationally invalid. Example: 'knowledge is apprehension of the known' is circular.
The definition must use new words different from the defined.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اجتناب الغموض ومظنته فيه : الجدل مهمة الحد أو التعريف هي الإيضاح والبيان، فنحن نعرف مصطلحا ما أو عبارة لكي نكشف عن معناها ونوضح المراد منها . ما، لكي وهذا يقتضي بداهة أن تكون العبارات المستعملة في التعريف عبارات واضحة لا لبس فيها ولا غموض، وإلا كانت سببًا في زيادة الإبهام والخفاء بدلا من أن تكون سببًا في البيان والتوضيح . يقول الطوفي : الحدود يجب أن يجتنب فيها الإبهام ومظنته كاللفظ المجمل والمجاز والغريب، خصوصا إذا لم يكن المجاز واضحا»(1) فمن شرط الحد – إذا – أن يكون أجلى وأوضح من المفرد التصوري الذي نشرحه، فإذا كان قولنا الشارح (تعريفنا) أخفى من المفرد الذي نشرحه أو مماثلاً الخفاء، فإن المخاطب لن يستفيد شيئا من شرحنا وتعريفنا، بل يبقى في جهالته ، ولا يستطيع أن يتصور هذا المفرد الذي نشرحه له عن طريق قولنا . يقول ابن النجار الفتوحي رحمه الله : في يجب مساواة الحد للمحدود، لأنه إن كان أعم فلا دلالة له على الأخص ولا يفيد التمييز، وإن كان أخص فلأنه أخفى، لأنه أقل وجودًا منه، ويجب أيضًا أن لا يكون في لفظه مجاز ولا مشترك، لأن الحد مميز للمحدود، ولا يحصل الميز مع واحد منهما» (3) وما ذلك إلا لأن الاشتراك مخل بفهم المعنى المقصود، كما أن الغالب تبادر المعاني الحقيقية إلى الفهم دون المجازية (4) ج - ألا يتوقف فهم التعريف على معرفة سابقة بالمعرف: ينبغي في التعريف أن نستعمل ألفاظا جديدة مباينة للفظ الذي نريد حده أو تعريفه، لأننا إذا استعملنا لفظًا من نفس مادة المصطلح المراد تعريفه نكون كمن يدور على نفسه، وكمن أراد تعريف الماء فقال إنه الماء . لذلك كان من الضروري أن لا يتوقف العلم بالتعريف على العلم بالمعرف وإلا لزم الدور، وهو ممنوع عقلا كتعريف العلم بأنه إدراك المعلوم، وذلك لأنه لا يعرف المعلوم حتى يعرف العلم فكيف يدخل المعلوم في تعريف العلم ؛ فهو إذا تعريف غير صحيح»
Avoiding ambiguity and its likelihood in it: The task of definition (hadd or ta'rif) is clarification and explanation. We define a term or phrase to reveal its meaning and clarify what is intended. This necessarily requires that the expressions used in the definition be clear, without ambiguity or obscurity; otherwise they would cause increased obscurity and concealment instead of being a cause of clarification and explanation. Al-Tufi says: 'Definitions must avoid ambiguity and its likelihood, such as the ambiguous word (mujmal), metaphor (majaz), and strange (gharib) usage, especially if the metaphor is not clear.' So a condition of definition is that it be clearer and more obvious than the conceptual singular (al-mufrad al-tasawwuri) we are explaining. If our explanatory statement (our definition) is more obscure than the singular we are explaining or equally obscure, then the addressee will gain nothing from our explanation and definition; rather, he remains in his ignorance and cannot conceive of this singular through our statement. Ibn al-Najjar al-Futuhi (may Allah have mercy on him) says: 'The definition must be equivalent to the defined; because if it is more general, it does not indicate the more specific and does not provide discrimination; and if it is more specific, it is more obscure because it is less existent than it. It is also necessary that there be no metaphor (majaz) or homonymy (mushtarak) in its wording, because the definition distinguishes the defined, and discrimination is not achieved with either of them.' This is only because homonymy impairs understanding of the intended meaning, and because true meanings are predominantly the first to come to mind, not metaphorical ones. (c) The understanding of the definition should not depend on prior knowledge of the defined: It is necessary in the definition to use new words different from the word we intend to define, because if we use a word from the same root as the term to be defined, we are like someone going in circles, like someone who wants to define water and says 'it is water.' Therefore, it is necessary that knowledge of the definition not depend on knowledge of the defined, otherwise circularity (dawr) would occur, which is rationally prohibited, such as defining knowledge ('ilm) as 'apprehension of the known (ma'lum).' That is because the known is not known until knowledge is known, so how can the known be included in the definition of knowledge? It is therefore an invalid definition.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage, from the book Jadal Usuliyyin, discusses the essential conditions that a valid definition (hadd or ta'rif) must fulfill in the context of dialectic (jadal). The author begins by affirming that the purpose of definition is clarification and explanation. To achieve this, the expressions used in the definition must themselves be clear, free from ambiguity and obscurity. If the definition is as obscure as or more obscure than the term being defined, it fails its purpose. The author then quotes al-Tufi, who lists specific linguistic pitfalls to avoid: ambiguous words (mujmal), metaphors (majaz), and strange (gharib) usages, especially when the metaphor is not obvious. Next, the author cites Ibn al-Najjar al-Futuhi, who adds two more conditions: the definition must be coextensive with the defined (not broader or narrower), and its wording must contain neither metaphor nor homonymy (ishtirak). The reasoning is that homonymy (a single word with multiple meanings) undermines the distinguishing function of definition, and metaphorical meanings are secondary to literal ones, causing confusion. Finally, the author presents a third condition: the definition must not rely on prior knowledge of the defined, otherwise it leads to circularity (dawr). An example is given: defining 'knowledge' as 'apprehension of the known' is invalid because knowing the known presupposes knowing knowledge itself. In Fiqh, a similar condition applies: if one defines 'wudu' as 'the act of using water on specific body parts,' one must not use 'water' in a way that itself requires definition of water. These conditions ensure that definitions are genuinely informative and serve as effective tools for resolving disputes in jadal.

Key Terms
الحد (al-hadd): A precise definition that distinguishes the defined from all others, consisting of genus and differentia or equivalent. [Note: In logic, hadd often contrasts with rasm (description); here it is used broadly for any definition.]
الإبهام (al-ibham): Ambiguity or obscurity that prevents clear understanding of the definition.
المجاز (al-majaz): Figurative or metaphorical language that diverts from the literal meaning; to be avoided in definitions unless obvious.
الاشتراك (al-ishtirak): Homonymy, where a single word has multiple distinct meanings, making it unsuitable for precise definition.
الدور (al-dawr): Circularity in definition, where understanding the definition depends on prior knowledge of the defined term.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is always metaphorical.
D) It is more general than the defined.

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must be clearer than the definiendum, neither more general nor more specific, literal, unambiguous, and independent of the definiendum itself.

Avoiding Circular Definitions in Islamic Scholarship
Author illustrates the fallacy of circular definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a circular definition (al-dawr) and explain why it is invalid in Islamic scholarly discourse.

Core Idea
A definition that presupposes what it defines leaves you spinning in circles.

One of the most basic errors in definition is circularity (al-dawr). The author illustrates this with two striking examples: defining a word by using the same root, and defining knowledge as 'apprehension of the known,' which presupposes what it tries to define. In this lesson, you will learn to spot such circular definitions and understand why they are unacceptable.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the term being defined and the definition given
Look at the author's first example: water is defined as 'water'. The definition uses the same word as the definiendum. In the second example, knowledge is defined as 'apprehension of the known'. Here the definition contains 'the known', which itself is known only through knowledge.
2
2. Check for circularity
Determine whether understanding the definition requires prior knowledge of the definiendum. In the water example, it's overtly identical. In the knowledge example, 'the known' cannot be known without knowledge, so the definition presupposes the very term it defines.
3
3. Explain why the definition is invalid
A circular definition provides no new information and leads to an infinite regress. The author calls it 'invalid definition'. In Islamic sciences, such definitions hinder clear understanding and cannot serve as a basis for debate.
4
4. Apply the test to a definition from an Islamic science
Consider the definition of 'riba' as 'any excess in a ribawi transaction'. If 'ribawi' is defined with reference to 'riba', it is circular. A valid definition should use independent terms, such as defining riba by the specific commodities and conditions mentioned in hadith.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تعريفه، لأننا إذا استعملنا لفظًا من نفس مادة المصطلح المراد تعريفه نكون كمن يدور على نفسه، وكمن أراد تعريف الماء فقال إنه الماء. لذلك كان من الضروري أن لا يتوقف العلم بالتعريف على العلم بالمعرف وإلا لزم الدور، وهو ممنوع عقلا كتعريف العلم بأنه إدراك المعلوم، وذلك لأنه لا يعرف المعلوم حتى يعرف العلم فكيف يدخل المعلوم في تعريف العلم؛ فهو إذا تعريف غير صحيح. المطلب الثالث: أهمية الحد أو التعريف في الجدل. مفاتيح العلوم مصطلحاتها ومصطلحات العلوم ثمارها القصوى، فهي مجمع حقائقها المعرفية وعنوان ما به يتميز كل واحد منها عما سواه، وليس من مسلك يتوسل به الإنسان إلى منطق العلم غير ألفاظه الاصطلاحية. لذلك تنطوي قضية المصطلح عند الأصوليين على أهمية بالغة، بل إنها تعتبر عندهم القضية الأساس في الدراسة الأصولية، فلا يكادون يتناولون قضية أصولية بالدراسة والبحث إلا وتكون أول مسألة يبدؤون بها فيها هي تحديد المصطلح الذي تدور عليه القضية كلها، وذلك ببيان المعنى الدقيق له عندهم، وذكر محترزاته والقيود التي تجعله جامعا لمواصفات موضوعه مانعا لدخول غيرها عليه - فالتعريف الاصطلاحي أو الحد كما يسميه الأصوليون - يشكل القضية الأولى التي يتناولونها بصدد دراستهم للمسائل الأصولية، وهذا لما أدركوه من أهمية لقضية المصطلح التي تصبح المحور العام للقضية المبحوثة كلها، ولا يمكن فهم القضية فهما واضحًا شاملا، إلا بعد الإحاطة بمعنى المصطلح الذي هو المحور الجامع والكلي لها. وإذا علمنا أن مسائل أصول الفقه قد دار حولها جدل كبير بين علماء أصول الفقه أنفسهم، عرفنا مدى الأهمية التي تنطوي عليها قضية المصطلح عندهم. فالجدل يقوم على التعامل مع المعاني التي يسهل معها الحوار بقدر ما تكون واضحة متميزة وبما أن تبادل المعاني لا يمكن أن يحصل إلا بواسطة الألفاظ، فإن الحاجة إلى ضبط دلالة الألفاظ وإلى تحديدها تصبح ماسة، ماسة، ويلزم من هذا أن الألفاظ المستعملة في الحوار ... يجب أن تكون واضحة محددة، ويكون من واجب المتحدث أن يحدد مدلولات ألفاظه ومن حق المستمع أن يطالبه بتحديد ألفاظه إن هو لم يحتط لذلك. ولا سبيل إلى تحديد مدلولات الألفاظ عند الحاجة إلا التعريف، الذي يلزم المتحدث بأن يقول: إني أعني باللفظ الفلاني الشيء الفلاني، إن كان المستمع لا يعرف مدلول اللفظ، أو طلب هو تحديد هذا المدلول أو فعل المتحدث ذلك احتياطا ودفعا لكل التباس ... إن تحديد الألفاظ ليس مطلوبا من المتحدث لكي يفهم حديثه غيره فحسب، بل هو مطلوب منه أيضًا لكي يلتزم المعنى الذي حدده لنفسه قبل أن يحدده لغيره، إنه ينبغي له ذلك لكي يقاوم ميله الطبيعي إلى الانحراف عن المعنى الذي يكون قد حدده بلفظ معين، وذلك بإقحام معنى آخر في اللفظ يعده مماثلا ومرادفا للمعنى الأول، كما ينبغي له ذلك لكي يمنع المستمع من الانزلاق من معنى إلى معنى آخر وراء اللفظة الواحدة. فالتعريف أو الحد ينطوي على أهمية بالغة بحيث لا يمكن القدح في هذه الأهمية ولا الانتقاص منها، وفي هذا قال ابن عقيل: قال قوم من الأصوليين: لا حاجة بنا إلى الحدود، ولا معنى لها، لأن الأسماء غناء عنها، لأنها أعلام على المسميات ... وهذا باطل، لأن في الحدود أكبر المنافع التي لا يوجد مثلها في الأسماء، فمن
Its definition: because if we use a word from the same material as the term intended to be defined, we are like one who circles upon himself, and like one who intended to define water and said: it is water. Therefore it was necessary that knowledge of the definition should not depend on knowledge of the definiendum, otherwise circularity would be necessary, and it is rationally prohibited, like the definition of knowledge as apprehension of the known, because the known is not known until knowledge is known, so how can the known enter into the definition of knowledge? Thus it is an invalid definition. Third topic: The importance of the limit (hadd) or definition in dialectics. The keys to the sciences are their terminologies, and the terminologies of the sciences are their ultimate fruits; they are the gathering place of their epistemic realities and the title of that by which each one is distinguished from others, and there is no path by which man may access the logic of science other than its conventional words. Therefore the issue of terminology among the Uṣūliyyūn carries immense importance; indeed they consider it the fundamental issue in Uṣūlī study. They hardly take up any Uṣūlī issue for study and research except that the first matter they begin with is the specification of the term around which the entire issue revolves, by clarifying its precise meaning according to them, and mentioning its exclusions and restrictions that make it comprehensive for the characteristics of its subject and prevent others from entering upon it. So conventional definition or limit (ḥadd) as the Uṣūliyyūn call it constitutes the first issue they address regarding their study of Uṣūlī questions, and this because they realize the importance of the issue of terminology, which becomes the general axis of the entire researched question; the question cannot be understood clearly and comprehensively except after grasping the meaning of the term that is the comprehensive and universal axis for it. And if we know that the issues of Uṣūl al-Fiqh have been subjected to great debate among the scholars of Uṣūl al-Fiqh themselves, we know the extent of importance that the issue of terminology carries for them. Dialectics is based on dealing with meanings that make dialogue easier to the extent that they are clear and distinct. Since the exchange of meanings cannot occur except through words, the need for controlling the signification of words and specifying them becomes urgent, urgent. From this it follows that words used in dialogue must be clear and specified, and it is the duty of the speaker to specify the significations of his words and the right of the listener to demand his specification if he has not taken precautions. There is no way to specify the significations of words when needed except definition, which obliges the speaker to say: I mean by such and such word such and such thing, if the listener does not know the signification of the word, or if he requests the specification of this signification, or if the speaker does that as a precaution and to prevent any confusion. Specification of words is not required from the speaker only so that others understand his speech, but it is also required from him so that he commits to the meaning he specified for himself before specifying it for others. He should do that to resist his natural inclination to deviate from the meaning he has specified for a particular word by introducing another meaning into the word that he considers similar and synonymous with the first meaning, and he should also do that to prevent the listener from slipping from one meaning to another behind the same word. So definition or limit carries immense importance such that one cannot disparage this importance nor belittle it. In this regard Ibn ʿAqīl said: A group of Uṣūliyyūn said: We have no need for definitions, and they have no meaning, because names suffice for them, for they are signs of the named... This is false, because in definitions there are the greatest benefits not found in names, for
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is an argument for the necessity and importance of definition (ḥadd or taʿrīf) in dialectical debate and in the Islamic legal methodology (uṣūl al-fiqh). The author begins by illustrating a common logical error: using the same word family in a definition, which leads to circularity. For example, defining water as 'water' is no definition. Similarly, defining knowledge as 'apprehension of the known' is flawed because it presupposes knowledge of the known, which itself requires knowledge. This demonstrates that definitions must avoid circularity (dawr).

The author then moves to the third topic: the importance of definition in jadal. He quotes that 'the keys to the sciences are their terminologies,' asserting that precise terminology is essential for scientific knowledge. For the Uṣūliyyūn (scholars of uṣūl al-fiqh), terminology is the foundational issue; whenever they study a problem, they first specify the key term, listing its exclusions (muḥtarazāt) and restrictions to make it comprehensive (jāmiʿ) and exclusive (māniʿ). This ensures that the term covers its proper subject and excludes what is not intended.

The author emphasizes that without a clear understanding of the central term, one cannot fully grasp the issue. He notes that the very debates among uṣūlī scholars themselves highlight the critical role of terminology. In jadal, clarity of meaning is paramount because dialogue requires precise exchange of concepts through words. Therefore, both speaker and listener have obligations: the speaker must define his terms, and the listener has the right to demand clarification. The author states that the only way to specify meanings when needed is through definition (taʿrīf).

Moreover, definition is not only for others but also for oneself—it forces the speaker to commit to a consistent meaning and resist the natural tendency to shift meanings. It also prevents the listener from equivocating. The passage concludes by citing Ibn ʿAqīl, who refutes the claim that definitions are unnecessary because names suffice. He argues that definitions provide immense benefits that names alone cannot, such as precision and avoidance of confusion.

الحد
التعريف
الدور

Key Takeaway
Circular definitions (dawr) fail because they assume what they are trying to define; a valid definition must stand on independent grounds.

The Central Role of Definition in Usul al-Fiqh and Dialectics
Author argues for the necessity of definition in usul al-fiqh and dialectics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why defining key terms is essential for productive scholarly debate in usul al-fiqh, based on the author's arguments.

Core Idea
In usul al-fiqh, the definition of a term is the axis around which every issue revolves.

The author argues that terminology is the key to sciences, and that Uṣūliyyūn always begin their study of an issue by defining the central term. This lesson explores why definitions are indispensable for both understanding issues and conducting disciplined debate (jadal). You will see how definitions serve both speaker and listener, ensuring clarity and preventing equivocation.

Guided Path
1
1. Recognize the claim: definitions are the first step in usul al-fiqh
The author states that Uṣūliyyūn never examine a question without first specifying the key term. This shows that definition is not optional but foundational.
The key term becomes the 'axis' (mihwar) of the entire discussion.
2
2. Understand the characteristics of a good definition: jāmiʿ and māniʿ
A proper definition includes all features of the subject (jāmiʿ) and excludes everything else (māniʿ). The author mentions 'muḥtarazāt' (exclusions) and 'quyūd' (restrictions) that achieve this.
3
3. Link definition to jadal (dialectics)
Dialogue relies on clear meanings; since meanings are conveyed through words, words must be precisely defined. The speaker has a duty to define his terms, and the listener has a right to demand definitions.
Without definition, debate becomes ambiguous and fails.
4
4. Recognize the dual benefit of definition for speaker and listener
Definition binds the speaker to a consistent meaning, resisting the natural tendency to shift meanings. It also prevents the listener from slipping from one meaning to another. Thus, definition maintains intellectual discipline.
Ibn ʿAqīl refutes the idea that names alone suffice because definitions provide benefits names cannot.

تعريفه، لأننا إذا استعملنا لفظًا من نفس مادة المصطلح المراد تعريفه نكون كمن يدور على نفسه، وكمن أراد تعريف الماء فقال إنه الماء. لذلك كان من الضروري أن لا يتوقف العلم بالتعريف على العلم بالمعرف وإلا لزم الدور، وهو ممنوع عقلا كتعريف العلم بأنه إدراك المعلوم، وذلك لأنه لا يعرف المعلوم حتى يعرف العلم فكيف يدخل المعلوم في تعريف العلم؛ فهو إذا تعريف غير صحيح. المطلب الثالث: أهمية الحد أو التعريف في الجدل. مفاتيح العلوم مصطلحاتها ومصطلحات العلوم ثمارها القصوى، فهي مجمع حقائقها المعرفية وعنوان ما به يتميز كل واحد منها عما سواه، وليس من مسلك يتوسل به الإنسان إلى منطق العلم غير ألفاظه الاصطلاحية. لذلك تنطوي قضية المصطلح عند الأصوليين على أهمية بالغة، بل إنها تعتبر عندهم القضية الأساس في الدراسة الأصولية، فلا يكادون يتناولون قضية أصولية بالدراسة والبحث إلا وتكون أول مسألة يبدؤون بها فيها هي تحديد المصطلح الذي تدور عليه القضية كلها، وذلك ببيان المعنى الدقيق له عندهم، وذكر محترزاته والقيود التي تجعله جامعا لمواصفات موضوعه مانعا لدخول غيرها عليه - فالتعريف الاصطلاحي أو الحد كما يسميه الأصوليون - يشكل القضية الأولى التي يتناولونها بصدد دراستهم للمسائل الأصولية، وهذا لما أدركوه من أهمية لقضية المصطلح التي تصبح المحور العام للقضية المبحوثة كلها، ولا يمكن فهم القضية فهما واضحًا شاملا، إلا بعد الإحاطة بمعنى المصطلح الذي هو المحور الجامع والكلي لها. وإذا علمنا أن مسائل أصول الفقه قد دار حولها جدل كبير بين علماء أصول الفقه أنفسهم، عرفنا مدى الأهمية التي تنطوي عليها قضية المصطلح عندهم. فالجدل يقوم على التعامل مع المعاني التي يسهل معها الحوار بقدر ما تكون واضحة متميزة وبما أن تبادل المعاني لا يمكن أن يحصل إلا بواسطة الألفاظ، فإن الحاجة إلى ضبط دلالة الألفاظ وإلى تحديدها تصبح ماسة، ماسة، ويلزم من هذا أن الألفاظ المستعملة في الحوار ... يجب أن تكون واضحة محددة، ويكون من واجب المتحدث أن يحدد مدلولات ألفاظه ومن حق المستمع أن يطالبه بتحديد ألفاظه إن هو لم يحتط لذلك. ولا سبيل إلى تحديد مدلولات الألفاظ عند الحاجة إلا التعريف، الذي يلزم المتحدث بأن يقول: إني أعني باللفظ الفلاني الشيء الفلاني، إن كان المستمع لا يعرف مدلول اللفظ، أو طلب هو تحديد هذا المدلول أو فعل المتحدث ذلك احتياطا ودفعا لكل التباس ... إن تحديد الألفاظ ليس مطلوبا من المتحدث لكي يفهم حديثه غيره فحسب، بل هو مطلوب منه أيضًا لكي يلتزم المعنى الذي حدده لنفسه قبل أن يحدده لغيره، إنه ينبغي له ذلك لكي يقاوم ميله الطبيعي إلى الانحراف عن المعنى الذي يكون قد حدده بلفظ معين، وذلك بإقحام معنى آخر في اللفظ يعده مماثلا ومرادفا للمعنى الأول، كما ينبغي له ذلك لكي يمنع المستمع من الانزلاق من معنى إلى معنى آخر وراء اللفظة الواحدة. فالتعريف أو الحد ينطوي على أهمية بالغة بحيث لا يمكن القدح في هذه الأهمية ولا الانتقاص منها، وفي هذا قال ابن عقيل: قال قوم من الأصوليين: لا حاجة بنا إلى الحدود، ولا معنى لها، لأن الأسماء غناء عنها، لأنها أعلام على المسميات ... وهذا باطل، لأن في الحدود أكبر المنافع التي لا يوجد مثلها في الأسماء، فمن
Its definition: because if we use a word from the same material as the term intended to be defined, we are like one who circles upon himself, and like one who intended to define water and said: it is water. Therefore it was necessary that knowledge of the definition should not depend on knowledge of the definiendum, otherwise circularity would be necessary, and it is rationally prohibited, like the definition of knowledge as apprehension of the known, because the known is not known until knowledge is known, so how can the known enter into the definition of knowledge? Thus it is an invalid definition. Third topic: The importance of the limit (hadd) or definition in dialectics. The keys to the sciences are their terminologies, and the terminologies of the sciences are their ultimate fruits; they are the gathering place of their epistemic realities and the title of that by which each one is distinguished from others, and there is no path by which man may access the logic of science other than its conventional words. Therefore the issue of terminology among the Uṣūliyyūn carries immense importance; indeed they consider it the fundamental issue in Uṣūlī study. They hardly take up any Uṣūlī issue for study and research except that the first matter they begin with is the specification of the term around which the entire issue revolves, by clarifying its precise meaning according to them, and mentioning its exclusions and restrictions that make it comprehensive for the characteristics of its subject and prevent others from entering upon it. So conventional definition or limit (ḥadd) as the Uṣūliyyūn call it constitutes the first issue they address regarding their study of Uṣūlī questions, and this because they realize the importance of the issue of terminology, which becomes the general axis of the entire researched question; the question cannot be understood clearly and comprehensively except after grasping the meaning of the term that is the comprehensive and universal axis for it. And if we know that the issues of Uṣūl al-Fiqh have been subjected to great debate among the scholars of Uṣūl al-Fiqh themselves, we know the extent of importance that the issue of terminology carries for them. Dialectics is based on dealing with meanings that make dialogue easier to the extent that they are clear and distinct. Since the exchange of meanings cannot occur except through words, the need for controlling the signification of words and specifying them becomes urgent, urgent. From this it follows that words used in dialogue must be clear and specified, and it is the duty of the speaker to specify the significations of his words and the right of the listener to demand his specification if he has not taken precautions. There is no way to specify the significations of words when needed except definition, which obliges the speaker to say: I mean by such and such word such and such thing, if the listener does not know the signification of the word, or if he requests the specification of this signification, or if the speaker does that as a precaution and to prevent any confusion. Specification of words is not required from the speaker only so that others understand his speech, but it is also required from him so that he commits to the meaning he specified for himself before specifying it for others. He should do that to resist his natural inclination to deviate from the meaning he has specified for a particular word by introducing another meaning into the word that he considers similar and synonymous with the first meaning, and he should also do that to prevent the listener from slipping from one meaning to another behind the same word. So definition or limit carries immense importance such that one cannot disparage this importance nor belittle it. In this regard Ibn ʿAqīl said: A group of Uṣūliyyūn said: We have no need for definitions, and they have no meaning, because names suffice for them, for they are signs of the named... This is false, because in definitions there are the greatest benefits not found in names, for
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is an argument for the necessity and importance of definition (ḥadd or taʿrīf) in dialectical debate and in the Islamic legal methodology (uṣūl al-fiqh). The author begins by illustrating a common logical error: using the same word family in a definition, which leads to circularity. For example, defining water as 'water' is no definition. Similarly, defining knowledge as 'apprehension of the known' is flawed because it presupposes knowledge of the known, which itself requires knowledge. This demonstrates that definitions must avoid circularity (dawr).

The author then moves to the third topic: the importance of definition in jadal. He quotes that 'the keys to the sciences are their terminologies,' asserting that precise terminology is essential for scientific knowledge. For the Uṣūliyyūn (scholars of uṣūl al-fiqh), terminology is the foundational issue; whenever they study a problem, they first specify the key term, listing its exclusions (muḥtarazāt) and restrictions to make it comprehensive (jāmiʿ) and exclusive (māniʿ). This ensures that the term covers its proper subject and excludes what is not intended.

The author emphasizes that without a clear understanding of the central term, one cannot fully grasp the issue. He notes that the very debates among uṣūlī scholars themselves highlight the critical role of terminology. In jadal, clarity of meaning is paramount because dialogue requires precise exchange of concepts through words. Therefore, both speaker and listener have obligations: the speaker must define his terms, and the listener has the right to demand clarification. The author states that the only way to specify meanings when needed is through definition (taʿrīf).

Moreover, definition is not only for others but also for oneself—it forces the speaker to commit to a consistent meaning and resist the natural tendency to shift meanings. It also prevents the listener from equivocating. The passage concludes by citing Ibn ʿAqīl, who refutes the claim that definitions are unnecessary because names suffice. He argues that definitions provide immense benefits that names alone cannot, such as precision and avoidance of confusion.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why do the Uṣūliyyūn begin their study of an issue with a definition of the key term?
A) Because definitions are easier to memorize than names.
B) Because the key term is the comprehensive axis of the issue, and without clear definition, the issue cannot be properly understood.
C) Because definitions are required by logic as a necessary precondition for any discussion.
D) Because the Uṣūliyyūn reject the use of names altogether.

Key Takeaway
Definition is the foundational step in usul al-fiqh and dialectics because it clarifies the axis term, enables precise debate, and disciplines both speaker and listener.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Open any usul al-fiqh textbook (e.g., al-Risala by al-Shafi'i). Find the first chapter and identify the key term being defined. Write down the definition and note whether it includes jāmiʿ and māniʿ features.
?
In a jadal exercise, take the definition of 'ijma' (consensus). Write a short dialogue where one person (mudda'i) asserts a definition, and another (mu'tarid) demands a clearer definition. Then have the mudda'i provide one that is comprehensive and exclusive.

The Necessity of Definition in Dialectic
Author argues for the necessity of definition in dialectic, citing Ibn 'Aqil, al-Mazari, and others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the dialectical role of definition in Islamic scholarly debate and evaluate the arguments for its necessity.

Core Idea
Definition is the guardian of meaning in dialectic; without it, even the most learned fall into ambiguity.

This passage tackles a fundamental question: do we really need definitions? Some early usulis thought names alone were sufficient. The author, citing Ibn 'Aqil and others, demonstrates why definitions are indispensable—not just for others, but for the speaker's own consistency, and for uncovering the causes behind terms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the thesis
The author opens by stating that dialectic depends on clear meanings conveyed through words, and thus words must be defined. Recognize that this is the central claim: definition is essential.
2
Recognize the objection
Some usulis argue that definitions are unnecessary because names are sufficient signs for things. This is the opposing view that the author refutes.
3
Analyze Ibn 'Aqil's rebuttal
Ibn 'Aqil provides two benefits of definitions: (1) they distinguish literal from metaphorical usage, and (2) they reveal the cause ('illa) behind a name, as in the example of 'wise' (hakim). Understand how these benefits address the objection.
The example shows that the definition of 'wise' as 'a quality that necessitates mastery of actions' clarifies its meaning and prevents confusion.
4
Examine al-Mazari's nuance
Al-Mazari adds that definitions are required for teaching others, but not necessarily for personal understanding if the reality is already grasped. Note how this refines the argument.
This shows that the necessity may be context-dependent, but does not undermine the overall importance.
5
Apply to an Islamic science
Consider how this principle applies in Usul al-Fiqh. For example, defining 'salah' (prayer) as 'specific acts and words beginning with takbir and ending with taslim' is essential to distinguish valid prayer from other acts. Without this definition, rulings could be confused.
This demonstrates the practical impact of the lesson's core idea.

فالجدل يقوم على التعامل مع المعاني التي يسهل معها الحوار بقدر ما تكون واضحة متميزة وبما أن تبادل المعاني لا يمكن أن يحصل إلا بواسطة الألفاظ، فإن الحاجة إلى ضبط دلالة الألفاظ وإلى تحديدها تصبح ماسة، ويلزم من هذا أن الألفاظ المستعملة في الحوار يجب أن تكون واضحة محددة، ويكون من واجب المتحدث أن يحدد مدلولات ألفاظه ومن حق المستمع أن يطالبه بتحديد ألفاظه إن هو لم يحتط لذلك. ولا سبيل إلى تحديد مدلولات الألفاظ عند الحاجة إلا التعريف، الذي يلزم المتحدث بأن يقول : إني أعني باللفظ الفلاني الشيء الفلاني، إن كان المستمع لا يعرف مدلول اللفظ، أو طلب هو تحديد هذا المدلول أو فعل المتحدث ذلك احتياطا ودفعا لكل التباس ... إن تحديد الألفاظ ليس مطلوبا من المتحدث لكي يفهم حديثه غيره فحسب، بل هو مطلوب منه أيضًا لكي يلتزم المعنى الذي حدده لنفسه قبل أن يحدده لغيره، إنه ينبغي له ذلك لكي يقاوم ميله الطبيعي إلى الانحراف عن المعنى الذي يكون قد حدده بلفظ معين، وذلك بإقحام معنى آخر في اللفظ يعده مماثلا ومرادفا للمعنى الأول، كما ينبغي له ذلك لكي يمنع المستمع من الانزلاق من معنى إلى معنى آخر وراء اللفظة الواحدة. فالتعريف أو الحد ينطوي على أهمية بالغة بحيث لا يمكن القدح في هذه الأهمية ولا الانتقاص منها، وفي هذا قال ابن عقيل: قال قوم من الأصوليين: لا حاجة بنا إلى الحدود، ولا معنى لها، لأن الأسماء غناء عنها، لأنها أعلام على المسميات . . وهذا باطل، لأن في الحدود أكبر المنافع التي لا يوجد مثلها في الأسماء، فمن ذلك أن الاسم قد يستعمل عن جهة الاستعارة والمجاز، فإذا جاء الحد، بين الاستعارة والمجاز من الحقيقة، فتعظم المنفعة، لأن كثيرا منه قد يلتبس ويشكل فيحتاج فيه إلى نظر واستدلال، ومن ذلك أنه قد يتبين المحدود من طريق آخر، أن فيه ذكر العلة والسبب الذي لأجله استحق الاسم والصفة، فيظهر معناه بظهور علته مثل قولنا حكيم هو اسم، فإذا طلب الحد، ظهرت حقيقة الحكمة، فكانت كاشفة للعلة، مثل قولهم : هي صفة للمرء توجب إتقان الأفعال الصادرة عنه. ويرى الإمام المازري فيما نقله عنه الزركشي أن الحد إنما يحتاج إليه في التعليم للغير، وأما الطالب لنفسه إذا لاح له حقيقة ما يطلب صح طلبه، وإن لم يحسن عبارة عنه صالحة للحد، فلا يكون هذا شرطًا إلا في حق من أراد التعليم لا التعلم. وقال ابن النجار الفتوحي في تأكيد أهمية الحد وضرورته : وهو - أي الحد - أصل كل علم، قال الفخر إسماعيل أبو محمد البغدادي من أصحابنا : الحد على الحقيقة أصل كل علم فمن لا يحيط به علما، لا نفع له بما عنده وقاله أيضا غيره، وهو صحيح.
Dialectic is based on dealing with meanings; ease of dialogue depends on how clear and distinct they are. Since exchange of meanings can only occur through words, the need to control the significance of words and to define them becomes urgent. From this it follows that words used in dialogue must be clear and defined; it is the speaker's duty to define the meanings of his words, and the listener has the right to demand that he define them if he has not been careful. There is no way to define the meanings of words when needed except by definition (ta'rif), which obliges the speaker to say: 'By such-and-such a word I mean such-and-such a thing,' if the listener does not know the meaning of the word, or if he requests the definition, or if the speaker does so as a precaution and to prevent all ambiguity. Indeed, defining words is required not only so that others understand his speech, but also so that he himself adheres to the meaning he defined for himself before defining it for others. He must do this to resist his natural tendency to deviate from the meaning he had assigned to a particular word by inserting another meaning that he considers similar and synonymous with the first, and also to prevent the listener from slipping from one meaning to another behind a single word. Thus definition (ta'rif) or limit (hadd) is of immense importance such that this importance cannot be disparaged or diminished. Regarding this, Ibn 'Aqil said: 'A group of usulis said: We have no need for definitions; they are meaningless, because names suffice for them, since they are signs for the named things. This is false, because definitions have the greatest benefits that are not found in names. Among these: a name may be used metaphorically or figuratively; when the definition comes, it distinguishes metaphor and figurative usage from literal truth, so great benefit accrues, because much of that may be confused and become problematic, requiring examination and inference. Also, it may become evident from another angle that the defined thing includes mention of the cause and reason for which the name and attribute are deserved, so its meaning appears through the appearance of its cause. For example, we say 'wise' is a name; if the definition is sought, the reality of wisdom appears, revealing the cause, such as their saying: 'It is a quality of a person that necessitates mastery of the actions emanating from him.' Imam al-Mazari, as quoted by al-Zarkashi, holds that definition is needed only for teaching others; as for one who seeks knowledge for himself, if the reality of what he seeks becomes clear, his seeking is correct, even if he does not express it in a phrase suitable for a definition; this condition applies only to one who intends to teach, not to learn. Ibn al-Najjar al-Futuhi affirmed the importance and necessity of definition, saying: 'It—i.e., definition—is the foundation of every science.' Al-Fakhr Isma'il Abu Muhammad al-Baghdadi said: 'Definition is truly the foundation of every science; whoever does not comprehend it has no benefit from what he possesses.' Others also said this, and it is correct.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical argument for the necessity of definition (hadd) in discourse, especially in jadal (dialectic). It begins by explaining that dialogue depends on clear meanings, which are conveyed through words. Therefore, words must be clearly defined, and it is the speaker's duty to define his terms and the listener's right to demand that. The only way to define meanings is through definition (ta'rif), which obliges the speaker to state explicitly what he means. The passage then notes that defining terms is not only for the listener's understanding but also for the speaker to remain consistent and avoid slipping into different meanings. It also prevents the listener from misinterpreting. After establishing the importance, it refutes those who claim definitions are unnecessary because names suffice. Ibn 'Aqil is quoted: names can be used metaphorically or figuratively, causing confusion; definitions clarify the true meaning and reveal the cause (illa) behind the name. An example is given: the word 'wise' (hakim) — without a definition, its meaning is vague, but defining it as 'a quality that necessitates mastery of actions' clarifies its essence. Next, al-Mazari distinguishes between teaching and personal learning: definitions are essential for teaching but not strictly necessary for personal understanding if the reality is already grasped. Finally, Ibn al-Najjar and al-Baghdadi assert that definition is the foundation of all knowledge, emphasizing its centrality. The commentary highlights that definitions serve both to avoid ambiguity in debate and to uncover the causal reasoning behind terms.

Key Takeaway

The Epistemic Role of Definition (Hadd)
Author cites multiple scholars affirming the necessity of definition for knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why definition (hadd) is considered foundational to all Islamic sciences and identify its function in distinguishing literal truth from metaphor.

Core Idea
Definition is the key that unlocks the reality behind words, revealing the cause of an attribute.

In this passage, the author brings together several scholars who affirm that definition is not merely a classroom exercise but the very foundation of knowledge. He explains that words can mislead when used metaphorically, and definition restores clarity by exposing the cause (ʿilla) that makes a thing deserving of its name. Understanding why definition is so central will sharpen your own pursuit of knowledge in any Islamic discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem that definition solves
The passage says words are used metaphorically and ambiguously. What is the confusion that definition clears up?
2
Find the example of 'hakim'
How does defining 'hakim' reveal the cause (ʿilla)? What is the cause according to the definition given?
3
Distinguish between teaching and self-learning
According to al-Maziri, is definition equally necessary for both contexts? Why might a student grasp reality without being able to define it?
4
Extract the universal claim
Ibn al-Najjar and al-Baghdadi state that definition is the foundation of every science. What does this imply about the priority of definition in the curriculum of Islamic sciences?

ذلك أن الاسم قد يستعمل عن جهة الاستعارة ،والمجاز، فإذا جاء الحد، بين الاستعارة والمجاز من الحقيقة، فتعظم المنفعة، لأن كثيرا منه قد يلتبس وَيُشْكِل فيحتاج فيه إلى نظر واستدلال، ومن ذلك أنه قد يتبين المحدود من طريق آخر، أن فيه ذكر العلة والسبب الذي لأجله استحق الاسم والصفة، فيظهر معناه بظهور ،علته مثل قولنا حكيم هو اسم، فإذا طلب الحد، ظهرت حقيقة الحكمة ، فكانت كاشفة للعلة، مثل قولهم : هي صفة للمرء توجب إتقان الأفعال الصادرة عنه» (1) وهو (2) ويرى الإمام المازري فيما نقله عنه الزركشي أن الحد إنما يحتاج إليه في التعليم للغير، وأما الطالب لنفسه إذا لاح له حقيقة ما يطلب صح طلبه، وإن لم يحسن عبارة عنه صالحة للحد، فلا يكون هذا شرطًا إلا في حق من أراد التعليم لا التعلم (3) (4) وقال ابن النجار الفتوحي في تأكيد أهمية الحد وضرورته : وهو - أي الحد - أصل كل علم، قال الفخر إسماعيل أبو محمد البغدادي ) أصحابنا - : الحد على الحقيقة أصل كل علم فمن لا يحيط به علما، لا من نفع له بما عنده وقاله أيضا غيره، وهو صحيح )
That is because the word may be used metaphorically and figuratively. When definition comes, it distinguishes metaphor and figurative from the literal truth, so great benefit accrues, because much of it is ambiguous and problematic, requiring investigation and inference. And from that is that the defined thing may become clear from another path, that it contains the mention of the cause and reason for which it deserved the name and attribute, so its meaning appears by the appearance of its cause, like our saying: 'Hakim is a name.' When definition is sought, the reality of wisdom appears, thus it becomes revealing of the cause, like their saying: 'It is an attribute of a person that necessitates mastery of actions emanating from him.' (1) It is (2) And Imam al-Maziri sees, as al-Zarkashi reported from him, that definition is only needed for teaching others. As for the student learning for himself, when the reality of what he seeks becomes apparent to him, his seeking is correct, even if he cannot express it in a suitable definition. So this is not a condition except for the one who intends to teach, not to learn. (3) (4) And Ibn al-Najjar al-Futuhi said, emphasizing the importance and necessity of definition: 'It—i.e., definition—is the foundation of every science.' Al-Fakhr Ismail Abu Muhammad al-Baghdadi said: 'Our companions say: Definition is truly the foundation of every science; whoever does not have comprehensive knowledge of it has no benefit from what he possesses.' And others also said this, and it is correct.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage brings together several scholarly opinions on the necessity of definition (hadd). The author begins by explaining that the need for definition arises because terms can be used metaphorically, and definition clarifies their true literal meaning. He then gives an example: the word 'hakim' (wise) is a name; when we seek its definition, the reality of wisdom becomes clear and reveals the cause (the attribute that requires mastery of actions). Next, he quotes Imam al-Mazari's view that definition is primarily for teaching; a student can grasp the reality without being able to articulate a formal definition. Finally, Ibn al-Najjar and al-Baghdadi affirm that definition is the foundation of all knowledge: without it, one's learning is fruitless. The passage underscores the epistemic priority of definition in the Islamic scholarly tradition.

Key Terms
الحد
المجاز
العلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn al-Najjar al-Futuhi, what is the status of definition (hadd) in relation to knowledge?
A) It is a tool for debate only.
B) It is the foundation of every science.
C) It is only necessary for teaching.
D) It is optional for advanced scholars.

Key Takeaway
Definition (hadd) is the foundation of all Islamic sciences because it reveals the cause that makes a term or attribute what it is, separating literal truth from figurative ambiguity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Read the definition of 'al-ʿādāt' (custom) in Usul al-Fiqh. Identify the cause (ʿilla) that makes a custom a valid source of law, as revealed by the definition.

Definition for Teaching vs. Self-Learning
Author cites multiple scholars affirming the necessity of definition for knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the necessity of definition for teaching versus self-learning, and apply al-Maziri's insight to evaluate the role of definition in your own studies.

Core Idea
Definition is essential for teaching others, but a sincere seeker can grasp reality without being able to formally define it.

Imam al-Maziri makes a subtle but powerful point: the need for a precise definition applies primarily to those who teach. A student who has attained direct understanding of a thing's reality may not need to articulate a formal definition. This lesson explores that distinction and its implications for how we approach learning and teaching in the Islamic tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Maziri's position
What does he say about when definition is needed? Who needs it?
2
Understand 'ṭālib li-nafsihi' (the one who seeks for himself)
Why might such a person not need to express a definition? What is the criterion for correct seeking?
3
Contrast with the teacher (muʿallim)
Why must the teacher be able to define? How does this relate to the responsibility of conveying knowledge?
4
Apply to your own situation
If you are studying a concept in Islamic theology, do you need a formal definition to have true knowledge? According to al-Maziri, what is the condition for your seeking to be correct?

Combining Language and Terminology in Definition
Methodological principle: combining language and terminology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why usuliyyun begin definitions with the linguistic meaning and how it connects to the terminological meaning.

Core Idea
Definitions in usul al-fiqh always start with language because the terminological meaning is derived from it.

In Islamic legal theory, every term has a linguistic root that shapes its technical meaning. This lesson explores why scholars always cite the linguistic meaning before the terminological one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Find the term, such as 'fiqh', and note how the author presents it.
2
Extract the linguistic meaning
Look for the phrase 'in language...' to see the original sense.
3
Find the terminological meaning
Look for 'in Sharia...' and note how it relates to the linguistic meaning.
4
Understand the connection
Realize that the terminological meaning is derived from the linguistic one, either entirely or partially.
Al-Shirazi emphasizes that the linguistic reality must not be violated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الرابع منهج الأصوليين في التعريف يقم منهج علماء الأصول في الحد أو التعريف على جملة من القواعد المنهجية التي عادة ما نجدها مطردة في كل دراساتهم، وهي: أ - الجمع بين اللغة والاصطلاح : جرت عادة الفقهاء والأصوليين في مؤلفاتهم على العناية بإيراد المعاني اللغوية والاصطلاحية لما يسوقونه من مصطلحات فقهية أو أصولية، ولا يتركون هذا إلا نادرًا جدًّا، وهذا ما يؤكده الطوفي رحمه الله إذ يقول : الأصوليون والفقهاء جرت عادتهم أنهم إذا انتصبوا لبيان لفظ، بينوه من جهة كذا» (1) . اللغة والشرع فقالوا مثلا : الفقه في اللغة كذا وفي الاصطلاح الشرعي ويشير الإمام الشيرازي إلى أن هؤلاء العلماء إنما اعتنوا بإيراد مفاهيم المصطلحات في كل من اللغة والاصطلاح الأصولي أو الفقهي، لأن المعنى الاصطلاحي في العادة يكون مشتقا في أبعاده كلها أو بعضها من أصل معناه اللغوي، ولذلك يراد إبراز هذا المعنى اللغوي حتى يعرف مدى صلته بالمعنى الاصطلاحي . يقول الشيرازي : الشيء إذا كان له حقيقة في اللغة تحدد بأنه حكم شرعي، فلا بد أن يأتي بما تقتضيه حقيقته في اللغة ولا يجوز أن يخل بمعناه الذي وضع له، وإن ضممنا إليه في الشرع أوصافًا ليحصل لنا الغرض المطلوب ب - الاحتراز في التعريف : من عادة الأصوليين حين يعرفون مصطلحا ما أن يشيروا إلى قيود التعريف التي احترز بها عن دخول غير المعرف في التعريف، فيقولون «احترز بكذا عن كذا، فما معنى الاحتراز؟ قال الطوفي: «الكلام عليه في أبحاث :
The Fourth Topic: The Methodology of the Legal Theorists in Definition. The methodology of the scholars of usul regarding definition or description is based on a set of methodological principles that are usually found consistently in all their studies, and they are: A - Combining language and terminology: The custom of jurists and legal theorists in their works is to pay attention to citing the linguistic and terminological meanings of the jurisprudential or usuli terms they present, and they rarely omit this. This is affirmed by al-Tufi, may Allah have mercy on him, when he says: 'The legal theorists and jurists customarily, when they undertake to explain a word, explain it from the perspective of language and Sharia.' They say, for example: 'Fiqh in language is such and such, and in Sharia terminology...' Imam al-Shirazi indicates that these scholars paid attention to presenting the concepts of terms in both language and usuli or jurisprudential terminology, because the terminological meaning is usually derived in all or some of its dimensions from the origin of its linguistic meaning, and therefore this linguistic meaning is brought forth so that its connection to the terminological meaning is known. Al-Shirazi says: 'If a thing has a reality in language defined as a legal ruling, then one must bring what its linguistic reality necessitates, and it is not permissible to violate the meaning for which it was coined, even if we add to it in Sharia attributes to achieve the desired purpose.' B - Precision (al-ihtiraz) in definition: It is the custom of legal theorists when they define a term to point out the conditions of the definition by which they guard against the entry of what is not defined into the definition. They say: 'He guarded against such and such by saying such and such.' What is the meaning of ihtiraz? Al-Tufi said: 'The discourse on it is in the investigations...'
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage outlines the two key principles used by legal theorists (usuliyyun) when defining terms. The first is the combination of linguistic and terminological meanings. The author cites al-Tufi and al-Shirazi to show that definitions always start with the linguistic meaning, because the terminological meaning is derived from it. They explicitly state the linguistic sense first to clarify the connection. The second principle is precision (al-ihtiraz): when defining, they carefully add conditions to exclude unintended meanings. For example, if defining 'salat', they might say 'specific actions beginning with takbir and ending with taslim' to exclude mere supplication. The text ends with the beginning of al-Tufi's explanation of ihtiraz, indicating a more detailed discussion that follows in the original work.

Key Terms
الاصطلاح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Shirazi, what is the reason for presenting both the linguistic and terminological meanings of a term?
A) To show that the terminological meaning is derived from the linguistic
B) To make the definition longer
C) To follow a tradition
D) To confuse the reader

Key Takeaway
The usuli method ensures that Sharia definitions are grounded in language, preserving the original meaning while adding precision.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Look up the definition of 'wudu' in a usul textbook. Identify the linguistic meaning and the terminological meaning. How does the terminological meaning relate to the linguistic meaning?

Precision (al-Ihtiraz) in Definition
Methodological principle: precision (ihtiraz) in definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of ihtiraz in usuli definitions and construct a definition with proper conditions to exclude unintended meanings.

Core Idea
Ihtiraz is the key to precise definitions: it guards against including what is not intended.

Precision in definition is not just about what to include, but what to exclude. This lesson explains how usuliyyun use ihtiraz to add conditions that exclude unintended meanings.

Guided Path
1
Understand the term being defined
Identify the term and what it is intended to cover.
2
Find the conditions added
Look for phrases like 'احترز بكذا عن كذا' indicating what is being excluded.
3
Determine what is excluded
Each condition (qayd) is meant to exclude a possible misinterpretation.
For example, 'beginning with takbir' excludes supplication without takbir.
4
Verify inclusiveness and exclusiveness
Check that the definition includes all intended instances and excludes all others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
