Ihtiraz: The Fortress of Precision in Definitions
Author explains the second rule: ihtiraz, the use of qualifiers to exclude unintended meanings from definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify ihtiraz qualifiers in a definition from usul al-fiqh and determine what each qualifier excludes.

Core Idea
Ihtiraz: restrictive qualifiers in definitions are fortresses against logical error.

In usul al-fiqh, definitions are not just descriptive; they must be precise to avoid including or excluding the wrong things. This lesson unpacks the second rule of definition: ihtiraz, the art of adding restrictive qualifiers. By understanding how al-Razi and other jurists use qualifiers like 'shari'i' and 'practical', you will learn to spot the protective function of each term in a definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the defined term (al-mu'arraf)
Find the term being defined in the passage. In the example, it is 'fiqh' (الفقه). The definition should be a precise description that matches only that term.
2
Extract each qualifier (qayd)
List the words or phrases that restrict the meaning. In al-Razi's definition: 'knowledge' (العلم), 'of shari'i rulings' (بالأحكام الشرعية), 'practical' (العملية), 'inferred as to their specific instances' (المستدل على أعيانها), and 'not known necessarily from religion' (بحيث لا يعلم كونها من الدين ضرورة). Each qualifier narrows the scope.
Some qualifiers are implicit; look for terms that could be replaced by a broader category.
3
Determine what each qualifier excludes
The author tells us: 'knowledge of rulings' excludes self-evident knowledge (الذاتية). 'Shari'i' excludes knowledge of the proofs of fiqh (consensus, solitary hadith, analogy). For each qualifier, ask: 'What broader category does it cut out?'
The exclusions are often stated explicitly in usul works.
4
Verify that the definition becomes coextensive (musawi)
Check that the qualifiers together make the definition apply to all instances of fiqh and exclude everything else. If any qualifier is missing, the definition might be too broad or too narrow. In the example, the qualifiers successfully limit 'fiqh' to 'knowledge of practical shari'i rulings derived from specific evidence'.
This step ensures the definition meets the requirement of ihtiraz.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ب - الاحتراز في التعريف : من عادة الأصوليين حين يعرفون مصطلحا ما أن يشيروا إلى قيود التعريف التي احترز بها عن دخول غير المعرف في التعريف، فيقولون «احترز بكذا عن كذا، فما معنى الاحتراز؟ قال الطوفي: «الكلام عليه في أبحاث : الأول : في لفظ احترز، وهو افتعل من قولهم : تحرزت من كذا، واحترزت منه، إذا توقيته وأصله من الحرز ، قال الجوهري : هو الموضع الحصين، يقال: هذا حرز حريز ، ويقول المتكلم احترزت بكذا من كذا، أي صرت في حرز من أن يدخل علي ما يفسد كلامي من جهة طرد أو عكس، أو غير ذلك. الثاني : في معنى الاحتراز في الكلام ،وكيفيته وذلك أن الألفاظ جعلت دالة على المعاني والمسميات وشأن الدليل أن يطابق المدلول، والمعرف أن يطابق المعرف، أي يكون طبقه ومساويًا له في العموم والخصوص، ولما كانت أجناس الأشياء شاملة لأنواعها وأنواعها شاملة لأشخاصها، وكانت الأجناس والأنواع متعددة، منها العالي والسافل والمتوسط .. والأشخاص أيضا متشابهة ومتباينة بالصفات، وكانت الأشخاص شائعة في أنواعها، والأنواع شائعة في أجناسها، لا جرم وجب على من أراد الكشف عن حقيقة شخص من نوع، أو نوع من جنس؛ أن يصفه بصفات مطابقة لا توجد إلا فيه ولا يتصف بها إلا هو، فكلما قلت أوصافه كان أدخل في العموم والشيوع والاشتباه وكلما كثرت أوصافه قرب من الكشف والتعين وزوال الاشتباه بغيره وقل ما يشتبه به من نوعه أو جنسه، فكان كل وصف من تلك الأوصاف المخصصة محصنا له من طائفة مما يشابهه أو يشتبه به وحرزًا له منه فهذا بيان كيفية الاحتراز . . . » (1) . من نماذج هذا المنهج عند الأصوليين، ما عرف به الرازي «الفقه»، حيث قال : عبارة عن (فهم المتكلم من كلامه . - وأما الفقه، فهو - في أصل اللغة وفي اصطلاح العلماء عبارة عن العلم» بالأحكام الشرعية، العملية، المستدل على أعيانها، بحيث لا يعلم كونها من الدين ضرورة . . . وقولنا العلم بالأحكام ؛ احترز عن العلم بالذاتية. وقولنا «الشرعية» ؛ احتراز عن العلم بكون الإجماع وخبر الواحد والقياس حجة، فإن كل ذلك أحكام شرعية مع أن العلم بها ليس من الفقه، لأن العلم بها ليس علما بكيفية عمل .
B) Ihtiraz in definition: It is the habit of usuliyyun when they define a term that they point to the restrictions of the definition by which they guard against the entry of what is not defined into the definition, saying 'He guarded by such-and-such against such-and-such.' So what is the meaning of ihtiraz? Al-Tufi said: 'Discussion on it entails several investigations: First, concerning the word ihtiraz: it is ifti'al from their saying: taharraztu from something, and ihtaraztu from it, when you avoid it. Its origin is from al-hirz. Al-Jawhari said: it is a fortified place. It is said: this is a safe fortress. The speaker says: I guarded by such-and-such from such-and-such, meaning I put myself in a fortress to prevent anything that would ruin my speech in terms of inclusion or exclusion or otherwise from entering upon me. Second, concerning the meaning of ihtiraz in speech and its modality: that words are made to indicate meanings and named things, and it is the nature of the proof (dalil) to correspond to the proved (madlul), and of the definer (mu'arraf) to correspond to the defined (mu'arraf), i.e., be coextensive and equal to it in generality and specificity. And since genera include their species and species include their individuals, and genera and species are numerous, including the higher, lower, and intermediate... and individuals also are similar and different in attributes, and individuals are common in their species and species common in their genera, undoubtedly it is necessary for one who wishes to uncover the reality of an individual of a species, or a species of a genus, to describe it with attributes that are coextensive, not found except in it and not characterized by them except it. Thus the fewer its attributes, the more it enters into generality, commonness, and confusion; and the more its attributes, the closer it comes to uncovering and specification and the removal of confusion with others, and the fewer things similar to it from its species or genus. So each of those specifying attributes is a fortress for it against a group of things that resemble it or are confused with it, and a guard for it from them. This is the explanation of the modality of ihtiraz...' Among the examples of this method of the usuliyyun is what al-Razi defined as 'fiqh' when he said: 'It is the theologian's understanding from his speech' - and as for fiqh, in its original language and in the terminology of the scholars, it is knowledge of shari'i practical rulings, inferred as to their specific instances, such that it is not known necessarily to be from the religion... Our saying 'knowledge of rulings' guards against knowledge of the self-evident. And our saying 'shari'i' guards against knowledge that consensus, solitary hadith, and analogy are proofs, for all of these are shari'i rulings but knowledge of them is not fiqh, because knowledge of them is not knowledge of how to act.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage explains the second rule: ihtiraz (cautious exclusion) in definitions. The author first defines the term ihtiraz linguistically, quoting al-Tufi and al-Jawhari, showing it means to avoid or fortify. Then he discusses its application: definitions must precisely match the defined, using attributes that are exclusive to it. Fewer attributes cause confusion; more attributes bring clarity. The author then gives an example from al-Razi's definition of fiqh, where al-Razi uses phrases like 'knowledge of rulings' and 'shari'i' to exclude non-fiqh matters such as self-evident knowledge or knowledge of the proofs of fiqh. This demonstrates how qualifiers are used to exclude what is not part of the definition.

Key Terms

الحرز

Key Takeaway
Ihtiraz is the use of restrictive qualifiers in definitions to exclude unintended meanings, each qualifier acting as a fortress against logical error.

The Fortress of Definitions: Ihtiraz
Author explains the linguistic and conceptual meaning of ihtiraz in definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose and mechanism of ihtiraz in definitions and apply it to evaluate whether a definition is coextensive.

Core Idea
Ihtiraz is the fortress that guards a definition against including what it should not.

In this passage, the author unpacks the linguistic root and technical function of ihtiraz, a key concept in definition theory. Understanding ihtiraz is essential for crafting definitions that are precise and coextensive with the definiendum, as used in usul al-fiqh and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Understand the linguistic origin
Ihtiraz comes from hirz (fortress). The author cites al-Jawhari: a fortified place. The speaker says 'I guarded against such-and-such' meaning I became in a fortress against corruption of my speech. This metaphor of protection is the foundational image.
2
Identify the purpose of ihtiraz in definitions
Words indicate meanings; a definition must correspond exactly (coextensive) with the definiendum. Ihtiraz ensures the definition applies only to the intended thing by adding specifying attributes.
Coextensive means equal in generality and specificity.
3
Examine the relationship between attributes and precision
Fewer attributes lead to generality and ambiguity; more attributes increase precision and remove ambiguity. Each specifying attribute (wasf mukhasis) is a fortress against confusion with similar items.
The author states: 'كلما قلت أوصافه كان أدخل في العموم... كلما كثرت أوصافه قرب من الكشف والتعيين'.
4
Apply the concept to a given definition
Given a definition, identify the parts that serve as ihtiraz—those attributes that exclude unintended items. For example, in the definition of 'salah', the phrase 'specific acts and sayings' excludes general supplication.
This step is crucial for evaluating whether a definition is sound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول : في لفظ احترز، وهو افتعل من قولهم : تحرزت من كذا، واحترزت منه، إذا توقيته وأصله من الحرز ، قال الجوهري : هو الموضع الحصين، يقال: هذا حرز حريز ، ويقول المتكلم احترزت بكذا من كذا، أي صرت في حرز من أن يدخل علي ما يفسد كلامي من جهة طرد أو عكس، أو غير ذلك. الثاني : في معنى الاحتراز في الكلام ،وكيفيته وذلك أن الألفاظ جعلت دالة على المعاني والمسميات وشأن الدليل أن يطابق المدلول، والمعرف أن يطابق المعرف، أي يكون طبقه ومساويًا له في العموم والخصوص، ولما كانت أجناس الأشياء شاملة لأنواعها وأنواعها شاملة لأشخاصها، وكانت الأجناس والأنواع متعددة، منها العالي والسافل والمتوسط .. والأشخاص أيضا متشابهة ومتباينة بالصفات، وكانت الأشخاص شائعة في أنواعها، والأنواع شائعة في أجناسها، لا جرم وجب على من أراد الكشف عن حقيقة شخص من نوع، أو نوع من جنس؛ أن يصفه بصفات مطابقة لا توجد إلا فيه ولا يتصف بها إلا هو، فكلما قلت أوصافه كان أدخل في العموم والشيوع والاشتباه وكلما كثرت أوصافه قرب من الكشف والتعين وزوال الاشتباه بغيره وقل ما يشتبه به من نوعه أو جنسه، فكان كل وصف من تلك الأوصاف المخصصة محصنا له من طائفة مما يشابهه أو يشتبه به وحرزًا له منه فهذا بيان كيفية الاحتراز . . .
First: regarding the word ihtiraz, it is derived from their saying: 'I protected myself from such-and-such, and I guarded against it' meaning I avoided it, and its origin is from al-hirz (fortress). Al-Jawhari said: it is a fortified place; it is said: this is a secure fortress. The speaker says: I guarded against such-and-such by such-and-such, meaning I became in a fortress against whatever would corrupt my speech from the angle of coextensiveness or converse or otherwise. Second: regarding the meaning of ihtiraz in speech and its modality, that is because words are made to indicate meanings and named things, and the function of the indicator is to correspond to the indicated, and the function of the definer is to correspond to the defined, i.e., to be coextensive and equal to it in generality and specificity. And since the genera of things encompass their species, and their species encompass their individuals, and the genera and species are multiple—higher, lower, and intermediate—and individuals are also similar and different by attributes, and individuals are common in their species, and species are common in their genera, necessarily it is incumbent upon whoever wants to uncover the reality of an individual of a species, or a species of a genus, to describe it with matching attributes that exist only in it and are characterized only by it. So whenever its descriptions are fewer, it is more included in generality, commonness, and ambiguity; and whenever its descriptions are more numerous, it approaches uncovering, determinacy, and removal of ambiguity with respect to others, and what resembles it from its species or genus rarely is ambiguous with it. So each of those specifying descriptions is a fortress for it against a group of what resembles or is ambiguous with it, and a protection from it. This is the explanation of the modality of ihtiraz.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of ihtiraz (circumscription) as used in logic and definition theory. The author first explains the linguistic derivation: ihtiraz comes from 'taking refuge' or 'fortifying oneself' (hirz meaning fortress). Then he explains its technical meaning in definitions: words are signs for meanings, and a proper definition must be coextensive (musawi) with the definiendum. Because genera encompass species and species encompass individuals, and individuals share attributes, a definer must include sufficient specifying attributes (al-awsaf al-mukhasissa) to uniquely identify the definiendum. Adding more attributes increases precision and removes ambiguity; fewer attributes lead to vagueness and overlap. Each added attribute serves as a 'fortress' (hirz) against confusion with similar things. The author's example is from fiqh definitions but is general to any definition.

حرز

Key Takeaway
Ihtiraz is the logical mechanism of adding specifying attributes to a definition to ensure it is coextensive with the definiendum, using each attribute as a fortress against inclusion of non-intended items.

Al-Razi's Definition of Fiqh and the Role of Ihtirazat
Al-Razi defines fiqh with ihtiraz clauses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four ihtiraz clauses in al-Razi's definition of fiqh and explain what each excludes.

Core Idea
A precise definition is built by systematically excluding what it is not.

Al-Razi's definition of fiqh is a masterpiece of logical precision. It does not just say what fiqh is; it also says what it is not, through ihtiraz (circumscription) clauses. Each clause carves away a potential misunderstanding, leaving only the exact meaning intended. In this lesson, we will dissect the definition and each ihtiraz to see how they work together.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Genus and the Core Definition
Start by isolating the core statement: fiqh is 'knowledge of practical Sharia rulings'. The genus is 'knowledge' (ilm). Notice that the definition immediately adds qualifications.
The word 'ilm' is the broad category.
2
Extract Each Ihtiraz Clause
Read the Arabic carefully and locate the four ihtiraz phrases: 'al-ilm bi al-ahkam' (excludes intrinsic matters), 'al-shar'iyya' (excludes knowledge of proofs), 'al-mustadall' ala a'yaniha' (excludes muqallid knowledge), and 'bi haythu la yu'lamu kawnuha min al-din daruratan' (excludes necessary knowledge).
Each ihtiraz begins with 'qawluna' (our saying) in the original.
3
Determine What Each Clause Excludes
For each ihtiraz, ask: what would be wrongly included if this clause were missing? Write down the excluded category: (1) intrinsic knowledge (like knowing Allah exists), (2) knowledge of usul proofs themselves, (3) the muqallid's knowledge, (4) necessary knowledge of obvious obligations.
The author gives concrete examples for each.
4
Verify Completeness and Coextensiveness
Check if the definition now includes all instances of fiqh and excludes all non-instances. Could there be any fiqh not covered? Any non-fiqh still included? This is the test of a sound definition.
Al-Razi's definition is considered one of the standard definitions in usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الفقه، فهو - في أصل اللغة وفي اصطلاح العلماء عبارة عن العلم بالأحكام الشرعية، العملية، المستدل على أعيانها، بحيث لا يعلم كونها من الدين ضرورة . . . وقولنا العلم بالأحكام ؛ احترز عن العلم بالذواتية. وقولنا «الشرعية»؛ احتراز عن العلم بكون الإجماع وخبر الواحد والقياس حجة، فإن كل ذلك أحكام شرعية مع أن العلم بها ليس من الفقه، لأن العلم بها ليس علما بكيفية عمل . وقولنا المستدل على أعيانها؛ احتراز عما للمقلد من العلوم الكثيرة المتعلقة بالأحكام الشرعية العملية، لأنه إذا علم أن المفتي أفتى بهذا الحكم، وعلم أن ما أفتى به المفتي هو حكم الله تعالى في حقه، فهذان العلمان يستلزمان العلم بأن تعالى في حقه ذلك، مع أن تلك العلوم لا تسمى فقها، لما لم يكن حكم الله مستدلاً على أعيانها . وقولنا بحيث لا يعلم كونها من الدين ضرورة احتراز عن العلم بوجوب الصلاة والصوم فإن ذلك لا يسمى فقها، لأن العلم الضروري حاصل بكونهما من دين محمد ) صلى الله (1) .
As for fiqh, it is—in the original language and in the terminology of the scholars—an expression for knowledge of the practical Sharia rulings, concerning which one has derived evidence for their specific instances, such that it is not known necessarily to be from the religion. Our saying 'knowledge of rulings' is a circumscription against knowledge of intrinsic matters. Our saying 'Sharia' is a circumscription against knowledge that consensus, solitary report, and analogy are proofs; for all of those are Sharia rulings, yet knowledge of them is not fiqh, because knowledge of them is not knowledge of how to act. Our saying 'concerning which one has derived evidence for their specific instances' is a circumscription against the many knowledges of the muqallid related to practical Sharia rulings; because if he knows that the mufti gave this ruling, and knows that the mufti's ruling is the ruling of Allah Almighty regarding his case, these two knowledges entail knowledge that the ruling of Allah regarding his case is that, yet those knowledges are not called fiqh, since the ruling of Allah is not derived by evidence for its specific instances. Our saying 'such that it is not known necessarily to be from the religion' is a circumscription against knowledge of the obligation of prayer and fasting, for that is not called fiqh, because necessary knowledge is obtained that they are from the religion of Muhammad (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage presents al-Razi's famous definition of fiqh in his al-Mahsul. The definition is: 'knowledge of the practical Sharia rulings concerning which one has derived evidence for their specific instances, such that it is not known necessarily to be from the religion.' Then the author (who is likely the author of Jadal Usuliyyin) explains each ihtiraz clause. First, 'knowledge of rulings' excludes knowledge of intrinsic matters (like knowledge of Allah's existence—that is not fiqh). Second, 'Sharia' excludes knowledge of the proofs themselves (consensus, solitary report, analogy), because knowing that these are proofs is not fiqh. Third, 'concerning which one has derived evidence for their specific instances' excludes the knowledge of a muqallid (blind follower), who may know a ruling but does not have evidence for that specific instance. Fourth, 'such that it is not known necessarily' excludes matters known by necessity (like the obligation of prayer and fasting), which are not considered fiqh because there is no effort in deriving them. Each ihtiraz refines the definition to match the precise scope of fiqh as derived knowledge from evidence.

Key Terms
فقه
احتراز
مقلد

C) Because his knowledge is not of practical rulings.
D) Because he does not know the ruling is from Allah.

Key Takeaway
A definition in Islamic logic is not just a statement of essence but a precision tool that uses ihtiraz to exclude all non-instances.

Al-Juwayni's Definition of 'Amr and Its Ihtirazat
Author presents al-Juwayni's definition of 'amr and its ihtirazat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four ihtirazat in al-Juwayni's definition of 'amr and explain what each excludes.

Core Idea
A precise definition in usul al-fiqh uses ihtirazat to block every possible misinterpretation.

Al-Juwayni, a master of usul al-fiqh, defines 'amr (command) with remarkable precision. His definition is not a simple phrase; it is carefully constructed with four qualifiers (ihtirazat) that each rule out a potential confusion. By dissecting these qualifiers, we learn how to build airtight definitions in Islamic legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full definition of 'amr
Locate al-Juwayni's complete definition: 'Amr is the speech that necessitates by itself obedience of the commanded one to do the commanded thing.'
2
Analyze the first ihtiraz: 'speech'
The term 'speech' (al-qawl) distinguishes 'amr from non-speech, such as gestures or written signs. A command must be linguistic.
3
Analyze the second ihtiraz: 'necessitates'
The term 'necessitates' (al-muqtadi) distinguishes 'amr from other types of speech like statements or questions, which do not inherently demand action.
4
Analyze the third ihtiraz: 'by itself'
The phrase 'by itself' (bi-nafsihi) excludes commands that are expressions (ibara) requiring external convention to convey meaning. A true command conveys the demand intrinsically.
5
Analyze the fourth ihtiraz: 'obedience'
Mentioning 'obedience' (ta'a) distinguishes 'amr from supplication (du'a), which requests but does not demand compliance with authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ذلك أيضًا؛ ما عرف به الجويني مصطلح «الأمر»، إذ يقول : «الأمر هو القول المقتضي بنفسه طاعة المأمور بفعل المأمور به . فذكرنا القول يميز الأمر عما عداه من الكلام. وذكرنا المقتضي إلى استتمام الكلام يميزه عما عدا الأمر من أقسام الكلام. وقولنا : بنفسه، يقطع وهم من يحمل الأمر على العبارة، فإن العبارة لا تقتضي بنفسها، وإنما تشعر بمعناها عن اصطلاح أو توقيف عليها . وذكرنا الطاعة يميز الأمر عن الدعاء، من غير جزم في طلب الطاعة ) (2) .
And also from that is what al-Juwayni defined the term 'amr (command), as he says: 'Amr is the speech that necessitates by itself obedience of the commanded one to do the commanded thing. So we mentioned 'speech' to distinguish 'amr from what is not speech. And we mentioned 'necessitates' to complete the speech to distinguish it from other divisions of speech besides 'amr. And our saying 'by itself' cuts off the illusion of whoever interprets 'amr as an expression (ibara), for the expression does not necessitate by itself, but only indicates its meaning by convention or stipulation. And we mentioned 'obedience' to distinguish 'amr from supplication (du'a), which does not have certainty in demanding obedience.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage gives al-Juwayni's definition of 'amr (command) from his work al-Burhan. The definition is: 'Amr is the speech that necessitates by itself obedience of the commanded one to do the commanded thing.' Then the author explains each ihtiraz. First, 'speech' (al-qawl) distinguishes 'amr from non-speech (like gestures). Second, 'necessitates' (al-muqtadi) completes the speech and distinguishes 'amr from other types of speech (like statements). Third, 'by itself' (bi-nafsihi) eliminates the idea that 'amr is merely an expression (ibara) that requires convention to convey meaning; 'amr inherently demands action. Fourth, 'obedience' (ta'a) distinguishes 'amr from supplication (du'a), which may ask but not demand obedience. Each clause narrows the definition to the precise meaning of a command as understood in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
أمر
اقتضاء

C) To indicate that the command must be spoken aloud.
D) To show that the command is from a superior.

Key Takeaway
Al-Juwayni's definition of 'amr uses four ihtirazat to precisely exclude non-commands, demonstrating the importance of careful definition in usul al-fiqh.

The Definition of Fiqh: Excluding Taqlid and Daruriyat
Author explains the conditions for a legal ruling to be called fiqh, excluding taqlid and necessary knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two conditions that exclude taqlid and necessary knowledge from the definition of fiqh and explain why each condition is necessary.

Core Idea
Fiqh requires evidence-based derivation; it excludes blind imitation and self-evident truths.

This passage expands the classical definition of fiqh used in usul al-fiqh. The definition is not merely 'knowledge of rulings' but includes two key conditions that ensure only knowledge derived from evidence qualifies. Understanding these conditions helps distinguish the work of a mujtahid from that of a muqallid and from matters known by necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the complete definition
Locate the definition being expanded: 'Knowledge of practical legal rulings derived from evidence regarding their specific instances, such that it is not known of necessity to be from the religion.'
This definition is a composite from the two precautionary phrases.
2
Analyse the first condition: 'derived from evidence'
The phrase 'al-mustadall 'ala a'yaniha' excludes the muqallid. Even if a muqallid knows the ruling and believes it is from Allah, that knowledge is not fiqh because it relies on authority, not derivation from evidence for that specific case.
The passage explains that the muqallid has two pieces of knowledge that together necessitate knowing the ruling, but the derivation step is missing.
3
Analyse the second condition: 'not known by necessity'
The phrase 'la yu'lam kawunuha min al-din daruratan' excludes matters like the obligation of prayer and fasting, which are known by necessity (darura) and do not require ijtihad.
Daruri knowledge is self-evident and does not involve inference; thus it falls outside the scope of fiqh.
4
Connect to the concept of kasb
Fiqh is kasbi (acquired) knowledge that requires effort and reasoning. The two conditions ensure that only acquired, evidence-based knowledge is called fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقولنا المستدل على أعيانها؛ احتراز عما للمقلد من العلوم الكثيرة المتعلقة بالأحكام الشرعية العملية، لأنه إذا علم أن المفتي أفتى بهذا الحكم، وعلم أن ما أفتى به المفتي هو حكم الله تعالى في حقه، فهذان العلمان يستلزمان العلم بأن حكم الله تعالى في حقه ذلك، مع أن تلك العلوم لا تسمى فقها، لما لم يكن حكم الله مستدلاً على أعيانها. وقولنا بحيث لا يعلم كونها من الدين ضرورة احتراز عن العلم بوجوب الصلاة والصوم فإن ذلك لا يسمى فقها، لأن العلم الضروري حاصل بكونهما من دين محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم.
And our statement 'derived from evidence regarding their specific instances' is a precaution against [the knowledge] of the one who follows taqlid from the many sciences related to practical legal rulings, because if he knows that the mufti gave this ruling, and he knows that what the mufti gave is the ruling of Allah Almighty in his case, then these two items of knowledge necessitate the knowledge that Allah's ruling in his case is that, even though those sciences are not called fiqh, since Allah's ruling was not derived from evidence regarding its specific instances. And our statement 'such that it is not known of necessity to be from the religion' is a precaution against knowledge of the obligation of prayer and fasting, for that is not called fiqh, because necessary knowledge is obtained that they are from the religion of Muhammad (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage provides an expansion (sharh) of the definition of fiqh as formulated in the works of usul al-fiqh, such as al-Razi's al-Mahsul. The definition under discussion is: 'Fiqh is the knowledge of practical legal rulings derived from evidence regarding their specific instances, such that it is not known of necessity to be from the religion.' The author here explains the two precautionary conditions (ihtiraz) embedded in this definition. The first condition, 'derived from evidence regarding their specific instances' (al-mustadall 'ala a'yaniha), excludes the case of the muqallid (one who follows blindly). If a muqallid knows that a mufti gave a fatwa and believes that fatwa to be Allah's ruling, this knowledge is not considered fiqh because it is not based on direct derivation from evidence for that specific case. The second condition, 'such that it is not known of necessity to be from the religion' (la yu'lam kawunuha min al-din daruratan), excludes matters like the obligation of prayer and fasting, which are known by necessity (darura) and therefore do not require the effort of ijtihad. Thus fiqh is characterized as acquired knowledge (kasbi) that requires inference and evidence, distinguishing it from both blind imitation and axiomatic religious knowledge.

Key Terms
الفقه
المستدل على أعيانها
الضرورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the muqallid does not have certainty about the ruling.
B) Because the muqallid's knowledge is not derived from evidence regarding the specific instance.
C) Because the muqallid's knowledge is based on necessary knowledge.
D) Because the muqallid's knowledge is about non-practical rulings.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh is defined as evidence-based knowledge of practical rulings, excluding both taqlid and matters known by necessity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a person who knows that zakat is obligatory because it is widely known (tawatur). Is this knowledge considered fiqh according to the definition? Explain using the condition regarding necessary knowledge.
?
A student memorizes a fatwa from a scholar and firmly believes it is Allah's ruling. Does this count as fiqh? Why or why not? Refer to the condition regarding derivation from evidence.

Juwayni's Definition of 'Amr': A Precision Tool in Usul al-Fiqh
Author presents Juwayni's definition and explains each component's function.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each component of Juwayni's definition of 'amr' and explain how it excludes other concepts.

Core Idea
Every word in a Usul al-Fiqh definition is a filter.

Definitions in usul al-fiqh are not casual statements; they are carefully crafted to isolate exactly one concept. Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni's definition of 'amr' (command) is a masterclass in this precision. Each term is chosen to exclude something else, turning the definition into a logical sieve. In this lesson, we will dissect that definition and see how each component functions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full definition
Find Juwayni's complete definition of 'amr' in the Arabic text. Read it carefully: 'الأمر هو القول المقتضي بنفسه طاعة المأمور بفعل المأمور به'.
2
Break down each component
List the components: al-qawl (speech), al-muqtadi (the demanding), bi-nafsihi (by itself), al-ta'a (obedience), and the remaining phrase 'the commanded one to do the commanded act'. Understand what each contributes.
The definition contains five distinct elements.
3
Trace what each component excludes
For each component, identify what concept is excluded. For example, 'al-qawl' excludes non-verbal signals; 'al-muqtadi' excludes speech that does not demand action; 'bi-nafsihi' excludes conventional expressions (like 'ibara); 'al-ta'a' excludes supplication (du'a).
This step shows how the definition carves out exactly 'amr'.
4
Recognize the shift from earlier usul
Notice the innovation: Juwayni's emphasis on 'by itself' reflects the Ash'ari theory that speech has intrinsic meaning, contrasting with earlier Hanafi definitions that allowed conventional connotations.
This is a key theoretical shift in usul al-fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ذلك أيضًا؛ ما عرف به الجويني مصطلح «الأمر»، إذ يقول: «الأمر هو القول المقتضي بنفسه طاعة المأمور بفعل المأمور به. فذكرنا القول يميز الأمر عما عداه من الكلام. وذكرنا المقتضي إلى استتمام الكلام يميزه عما عدا الأمر من أقسام الكلام. وقولنا: بنفسه، يقطع وهم من يحمل الأمر على العبارة، فإن العبارة لا تقتضي بنفسها، وإنما تشعر بمعناها عن اصطلاح أو توقيف عليها. وذكرنا الطاعة يميز الأمر عن الدعاء، من غير جزم في طلب الطاعة) (2).
And among that also is what al-Juwayni defined with the term 'al-amr': he said: 'Al-amr is that speech which demands by itself the obedience of the commanded one to do the commanded act. So we mentioned 'speech' to distinguish al-amr from other speech. And we mentioned 'the demanding to the completion of speech' to distinguish it from other divisions of speech apart from al-amr. And our statement 'by itself' eliminates the illusion of those who interpret al-amr as a statement (ibara), for the statement does not demand by itself, but only indicates its meaning through convention or designation. And we mentioned 'obedience' to distinguish al-amr from supplication (du'a), which lacks decisiveness in requesting obedience.'
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage presents the definition of 'amr (command) as articulated by Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni in his work al-Burhan fi Usul al-Fiqh. The definition is: 'Al-amr is that speech which demands by itself the obedience of the commanded one to do the commanded act.' The author then dissects the definition into its components, each serving as a limiting condition. First, 'speech' (al-qawl) distinguishes command from non-verbal signals. Second, 'the demanding' (al-muqtadi) sets it apart from other types of speech that do not demand action. Third, 'by itself' (bi-nafsihi) excludes euphemistic expressions (al-ibara) that rely on convention for their meaning. Fourth, 'obedience' (ta'a) differentiates commands from supplications (du'a), where there is no firm demand for compliance. This careful partitioning shows how usul al-fiqh definitions are constructed to precisely capture the intended concept and exclude others.

Key Terms
الأمر (al-amr) - command
المقتضي (al-muqtadi) - the demanding aspect
العبارة (al-ibara) - statement by convention

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Juwayni's definition of 'amr', which component distinguishes it from supplication (du'a)?
A) al-qawl
B) al-muqtadi
C) bi-nafsihi
D) al-ta'a

Key Takeaway
Juwayni's definition shows that every term in a hadd serves to carve out the exact meaning, leaving no ambiguity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Construct a definition of another legal concept, such as 'prohibition' (al-nahy), following Juwayni's method: identify its genus, differentia, and what each component excludes.
?
Take a definition from a fiqh text (e.g., 'salah is a set of actions and utterances beginning with takbir and ending with taslim') and analyze it: what are the components, and what do they exclude?

First Type of Usuli Definition: Definition by Distinction (al-Ta'rif bi al-Tamyiz)
Author introduces the first type of definition used by usuliyyun: definition by distinguishing characteristics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the distinctive feature of 'definition by distinction' and explain why usuliyyun use it instead of essential definitions.

Core Idea
Definition by distinction separates things without revealing their essence—practical for fiqh.

Usuliyyun did not restrict themselves to essential definitions like the logicians. They adopted diverse methods, the first of which is 'definition by distinction' (al-ta'rif bi al-tamyiz). This lesson explores what this type is and why it is useful in legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context
The author states that usuliyyun did not follow a single pattern in definitions; they used diverse paths. This sets the stage for a classification of definition types.
This is a methodological observation, not a logical claim.
2
Extract the core requirement
Definition by distinction requires specifying sufficient characteristics (sifat) to separate the defined (al-mahdud) from others. It does not aim to describe the essence (haqiqa).
The phrase 'fasi' (separation) is key: it is about distinction, not essence.
3
Contrast with essential definitions
Unlike al-ta'rif bi al-hadd (essential definition), this type abstains from seeking characteristics that define the thing's essence in itself. It is a rasm (description) rather than a hadd haqiqi.
Essential definitions require genus (jins) and differentia (fasl); this type only needs sufficient differentiating marks.
4
Examine the example from al-Tufi
The author mentions al-Tufi's definition of al-mubah (the permissible) as an instance. Even though the text cuts off, we can infer that al-Tufi defined al-mubah by highlighting characteristics that distinguish it from other legal categories (wajib, haram, etc.) without stating its essential nature.
The incomplete example signals a typical usuli move: prioritizing functional demarcation over metaphysical inquiry.
5
Assess the practical advantage
In usul al-fiqh, definitions serve to delimit concepts for legal reasoning. Definition by distinction is efficient because it provides enough clarity to apply rulings without delving into philosophical essences.
This pragmatic approach aligns with the needs of jurists who require operative definitions for analogy (qiyas) and other proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الخامس : أنواع التعريفات عند الأصوليين لم يجر الأصوليون على طريقة واحد أو على نمط واحد من التعريفات وإنما سلكوا في التعريفات مسالك متنوعة، نذكر منها : أولا : التعريف بالتمييز : ومقتضاه، أن يعين للمحدود من الأوصاف ما يكفي لفصله عن غيره، من غير ما حاجة إلى طلب الأوصاف التي تعرف بها حقيقته في ذاتها (2) . ذلك ما أورده الطوفي في تعريف المباح : من .
The fifth demand: Types of definitions according to the usuliyyun. The usuliyyun did not follow a single method or a single pattern of definitions, but rather took diverse paths in definitions, among which we mention: First: Definition by distinction (al-ta'rif bi al-tamyiz). Its requirement is to specify for the defined thing sufficient characteristics to separate it from others, without the need to seek characteristics that define its essence in itself. That is what al-Tufi presented in his definition of al-mubah: from...
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage begins a classification of types of definitions employed by scholars of usul al-fiqh. The author, presumably the author of 'Jadal Usuliyyin', enumerates these types. The first type presented is 'definition by distinction' (al-ta'rif bi al-tamyiz). The defining feature of this type is that it does not aim to describe the essence (mahiyya) of the thing being defined; rather, it selects sufficient attributes (sifat) that enable one to distinguish the defined from other things. This is a practical approach suitable for legal definitions where knowing the essence is not always necessary. The author gives an example from al-Tufi's definition of al-mubah (the permissible), but the text cuts off. The example likely continues to show how al-Tufi defined al-mubah using distinguishing characteristics rather than a full essential definition.

Key Terms
التعريف بالتمييز (al-ta'rif bi al-tamyiz): Definition that specifies distinguishing characteristics to separate the defined from others, without describing its essence. [Note: This type is contrasted with 'al-ta'rif bi al-hadd' (essential definition) in logic; in usul it is often used pragmatically.]

Key Takeaway
Definition by distinction prioritises functional separation over metaphysical essence—a hallmark of usuli pragmatism.

Critique of Definitions of al-Bayan
Author presents and critiques three definitions of al-bayan, endorsing al-Qadi Abu Bakr's definition as proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to critique definitions of a key term in usul al-fiqh using the criteria of precision and adequacy, and distinguish between metaphorical, epistemological, and proof-based definitions.

Core Idea
A proper definition in usul al-fiqh must be precise, not metaphorical, and must survive counterexamples.

In usul al-fiqh, the term 'al-bayan' (clarification) is foundational. How we define it affects how we understand the process of divine and human communication of rulings. The author presents three competing definitions, showing why two fail and one succeeds. By examining his criteria, you will learn how to evaluate definitions in Islamic legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three definitions
Locate the three definitions of al-bayan in the Arabic passage. The first uses metaphorical language, the second equates it with knowledge, and the third with proof.
2
Analyze the first critique
The author rejects the first definition because it uses metaphorical terms like 'realm' and 'clarity', which are not precise. A definition should be a 'mold' that captures the essence without deficiency or excess.
Metaphors can be evocative but fail the logical requirement of univocity.
3
Analyze the second critique
The author provides two counterexamples: one can say 'the clarification is complete' even if the listener does not understand, and one can say 'I clarified but it was not clarified'. Thus al-bayan cannot be identified with knowledge, since knowledge implies understanding.
The counterexamples show a lack of necessary equivalence between al-bayan and knowledge.
4
Understand the endorsed definition
The author endorses al-Qadi Abu Bakr's definition: al-bayan is the proof (al-dalil). Proof is divided into rational and scriptural. This definition is precise and avoids the problems of the others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذلك إذ يقول رحمه الله : اختلفت عبارات الخائضين في هذا الفن في معنى (البيان): فذهب بعض من ينسب إلى الأصوليين إلى أن البيان إخراج الشيء من حيز الإشكال إلى حيز التجلي والوضوح. وهذه العبارة وإن كانت محومة على المقصود فليست مرضية، فإنها مشتملة على ألفاظ مستعارة كالحيز والتجلي، وذوو البصائر لا يودعون مقاصد الحدود إلا في عبارات هي قوالب تبلغ الغرض من غير قصور ولا ازدياد يفهمها المبتدئون ويحسنها المنتهون . وقال قائل : البيان هو العلم . . وهو غير مرضي، فإن الإنسان ينهي الكلام إلى حد البيان، ويحسن منه أن يقول : تم البيان وإن لم يفهم المخاطب، وقد يقول : بينت فلم يتبين . والقول المرضي في البيان؛ ما ذكره القاضي أبو بكر، حيث قال : البيان هو الدليل، ثم الدليل ينقسم إلى العقلي والسمعي والله سبحانه وتعالى مبين الأمور المعقولة بنصب الأدلة العقلية عليها، والمسمع المخاطب مبين للمخاطب ما يبغيه إذا استقل كلامه بالإبانة والإشعار بالغرض، فهذا منتهى المقصود في هذا الفن
And that is when he says, may God have mercy on him: The expressions of those engaged in this art have differed regarding the meaning of 'al-bayan'. Some of those attributed to the usuliyyin held that al-bayan is bringing a thing out from the realm of ambiguity into the realm of clarity and evidence. This expression, although it approaches the intended meaning, is not satisfactory, for it contains metaphorical words like 'realm' and 'clarity', and those with insight do not deposit the aims of definitions except in expressions that are molds that achieve the purpose without deficiency or addition, understood by beginners and approved by advanced scholars. And another said: al-bayan is knowledge... and it is unsatisfactory, for a person finishes speech at the point of al-bayan, and it is proper for him to say: 'the clarification is complete' even if the addressee does not understand, and he may say: 'I clarified but it was not clarified'. And the satisfactory view on al-bayan is that mentioned by al-Qadi Abu Bakr, where he said: al-bayan is the proof. Then proof is divided into rational and scriptural. And God, exalted, clarifies rational matters by erecting rational proofs upon them, and the hearing addressee clarifies to the addressee what he intends if his speech suffices for elucidation and indication of the purpose. So this is the ultimate aim in this art.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is a critical review of three definitions of the term 'al-bayan' (clarification/explanation) as used in usul al-fiqh. The author begins by stating that scholars have differed on the meaning. The first definition claims al-bayan is 'bringing something out from ambiguity to clarity'. The author critiques this as unsatisfactory because it uses metaphorical terms ('realm', 'clarity') which are not precise enough for a proper logical definition. The second definition equates al-bayan with 'knowledge'. The author rejects this because one can say 'the clarification is complete' even if the listener did not understand, and one can say 'I clarified but it was not clarified', showing that al-bayan is not identical to knowledge in the mind of the listener. The author then presents the view of al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, who defines al-bayan as 'the proof' (dalil). This is endorsed as satisfactory. The author explains that proof is divided into rational and scriptural. God clarifies rational matters through rational proofs, and a speaker clarifies to an addressee what he intends if his speech fully indicates the purpose. This ends the discussion on al-bayan. The examples used are from the Islamic science of usul al-fiqh, specifically concerning definitions of key terms.

Key Terms
البيان
الدليل
الحد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A satisfactory definition in usul al-fiqh must be precise, non-metaphorical, and immune to counterexamples that show lack of equivalence.

Three Methods of Definition in Usul al-Fiqh: Distinction, Opposite, and Example
Author enumerates three methods of definition used by usuliyyin: by distinction, by opposite, and by example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three methods of definition used by usuliyyin (definition by distinction, by opposite, and by example) and identify which method is employed in a given definition from usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Usuliyyin define terms using distinction, opposition, or example—not just strict logical hadd.

In usul al-fiqh, jurists often define key terms like al-mubah, al-makruh, and al-mandub without adhering to the strict genus-differentia structure of Aristotelian logic. Instead, they use three flexible methods: assigning distinguishing attributes, contrasting with opposites, or giving an example. This passage from a jadal/usul text classifies these methods, showing how definitions work practically in legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three methods
The passage explicitly names three methods: al-ta'rif bi al-tamyiz (by distinction), al-ta'rif bi al-didd (by opposite), and al-ta'rif bi al-mithal (by example). Note each one.
2
Understand the logic of each method
For distinction: assign sufficient attributes to separate the defined from others, without needing essence. For opposite: contrast with its opposite and affirm attributes negated from the opposite. For example: clarify meaning by citing a typical instance.
3
Analyze the examples given
Al-Tufi's definition of al-mubah (permissible) uses distinction: it is 'what the Lawgiver addresses with choice without replacement' – the phrase 'without replacement' distinguishes it from obligations with replacement. The definition of al-makruh (disliked) as opposite of al-mandub (recommended) uses opposition: one is non-categorical command, the other non-categorical prohibition. Al-Baydawi's definition of istiqra' (induction) uses example (though the text is cut off).
The third example is incomplete, but the method is clear.
4
Compare with logical hadd
Classical logical definition (hadd) requires genus and differentia to capture essence. These usuli methods are more pragmatic: they suffice for identifying the term in legal discourse without delving into essential natures.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المطلب الخامس : أنواع التعريفات عند الأصوليين لم يجر الأصوليون على طريقة واحد أو على نمط واحد من التعريفات وإنما سلكوا في التعريفات مسالك متنوعة، نذكر منها : أولا : التعريف بالتمييز : ومقتضاه، أن يعين للمحدود من الأوصاف ما يكفي لفصله عن غيره، من غير ما حاجة إلى طلب الأوصاف التي تعرف بها حقيقته في ذاتها . ذلك ما أورده الطوفي في تعريف المباح : قال الآمدي : هو ما دل الدليل السمعي على خطاب الشارع بالتخيير فيه (من غير بدل) . . قلت : احترز بقوله من غير بدل من الواجب الموسع والمخير وفرض الكفاية، فإن التخيير لاحق لها، لكن بشرط الإتيان بالبدل . ثانيا : التعريف بالضد أو بالتضاد : ومقتضاه ؛ أن يقابل بين المحدود وضده، وأن يثبت له من الأوصاف ما منفي عن ضده، والعكس بالعكس من غير ما حاجة إلى طلب الأوصاف التي تعرف بها مطابقته لذاته . من ذلك ما أورده الطوفي في شرحه على مختصره لروضة الناظر لابن قدامة : قوله : (المكروه ضد المندوب)، قلت: يظهر تضادهما على ما مضى في المندوب، وذكر هنا .. وقد ظهر من تقسيم الخطاب إلى الأحكام أن المندوب : المأمور غير الجازم، والمكروه المنهي غير الجازم، فالمندوب قسيم الواجب في الأمر، والمكروه قسيم الحرام في النهي، فتحققت الضدية بينهما من حيث الحقيقة والمادة أي من حيث حقيقتهما ومادتهما . ثالثا : التعريف بالمثال : ومعناه أن يكتفى في تعريف المصطلح بإيراد مثال له يبين معناه، دون الحاجة إلى إيراد حد خاص به، من ذلك ما عرف به البيضاوي مصطلح الاستقراء، حيث قال :
Fifth Demand: Types of Definitions According to the Usuliyyin. The usuliyyin did not follow a single method or a single pattern of definitions; rather, they pursued diverse approaches in definitions, among which we mention: First: Definition by distinction: Its requirement is that one assign to the defined object from the descriptions what suffices to separate it from others, without need to seek the descriptions by which its essence in itself is known. That is what al-Tufi presented in defining al-mubah (the permissible): al-Amidi said: It is that which scriptural evidence indicates is the address of the Lawgiver with choice concerning it (without replacement). I (al-Tufi) say: He guarded by his statement 'without replacement' against the expanded obligatory, the choice obligatory, and the collective duty, for choice attaches to them, but with the condition of performing the replacement. Second: Definition by opposite or by opposition: Its requirement is that one contrast between the defined and its opposite, and affirm for it the descriptions that are negated from its opposite, and vice versa, without need to seek the descriptions by which its conformity to its essence is known. Among that is what al-Tufi presented in his commentary on his abridgment of Rawdat al-Nazir by Ibn Qudama: His statement: (The disliked is the opposite of the recommended). I say: Their opposition appears as what preceded regarding the recommended, and he mentioned here... And it has appeared from the division of speech into rulings that the recommended is the non-categorical command, and the disliked is the non-categorical prohibition. So the recommended is the counterpart of the obligatory in command, and the disliked is the counterpart of the forbidden in prohibition. Thus the opposition is realized between them from the perspective of reality and matter, i.e., from the perspective of their reality and their matter. Third: Definition by example: Its meaning is that one suffices in defining a term by presenting an example that clarifies its meaning, without need to present a specific definition for it. Among that is what al-Baydawi defined the term 'al-istiqra'' (induction), where he said:
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage is a classification of three methods of definition employed by the usuliyyin (legal theorists). The author begins by noting that usuliyyin did not restrict themselves to one method; they used diverse approaches. First is definition by distinction (al-ta'rif bi al-tamyiz), which assigns enough attributes to separate the defined thing from others without needing to describe its essence. The example given is al-Tufi's definition of al-mubah (the permissible) building on al-Amidi: it is what scriptural evidence indicates is addressed by choice without replacement. The phrase 'without replacement' excludes types of obligations that involve choice but with replacement. Second is definition by opposite (al-ta'rif bi al-didd), which contrasts the defined with its opposite. The example is from al-Tufi explaining that al-makruh (disliked) is the opposite of al-mandub (recommended). He shows they are opposites because one is a non-categorical command and the other a non-categorical prohibition. Third is definition by example (al-ta'rif bi al-mithal), where a term is clarified by an example without a formal definition. The example is from al-Baydawi defining istiqra' (induction), though the quote is incomplete here. All examples are from Islamic legal theory (usul al-fiqh), illustrating how definitions function in that discipline.

Key Terms
التعريف بالتمييز
التعريف بالضد
التعريف بالمثال
المباح
المكروه
المندوب

Key Takeaway
Usuliyyin employ three definitional strategies—distinction, opposition, and example—that prioritize functional separation over essential definition.

Definition by Opposite in Jadal
Author explains definition by opposite with examples from Tufi and Lamishi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Islamic legal terms (like mandub, makruh) using the method of definition by opposite.

Core Idea
A term can be defined by contrasting it with its opposite through negation of shared attributes.

In jadal and usul al-fiqh, a term can be defined by identifying its clear opposite. This technique saves effort by using well-known opposites to convey meaning. The passage explains the method and gives two key examples from al-Tufi and al-Lamishi that illustrate how definition by opposite works in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Find the term that is defined by its opposite. In the examples, the terms are 'mandub', 'makruh', and 'jahl'. Note which one is the focus in each case.
2
Identify the opposite term
Locate the opposite (didd or naqid) explicitly paired with the term. For mandub, the opposite is makruh; for jahl, the opposite is 'ilm (knowledge).
The text uses 'naqid' for jahl, meaning contradictory opposite.
3
Determine the shared genus
Both the term and its opposite belong to a common category (jins). For mandub and makruh, both are types of legal rulings (ahkam) related to command and prohibition. For jahl and 'ilm, both are states of knowledge or belief.
The shared genus provides the basis for comparison.
4
Extract the differentiating attribute by negation
Note which attribute is affirmed for one and negated for the other. Mandub is commanded without decisiveness; makruh is prohibited without decisiveness. Jahl is the absence of knowledge, so knowledge is affirmed for 'ilm and negated for jahl.
The defining attribute is often a negation of the opposite's characteristic.
5
Verify the definition's completeness
Check if the definition by opposite captures the essence. The author affirms that the opposition between mandub and makruh is in terms of reality and matter, implying the definition is sound for jadal purposes.
The passage notes that definition by opposite can suffice without seeking direct essential attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثانيا : التعريف بالضد أو بالتضاد : هو ومقتضاه ؛ أن يقابل بين المحدود وضده، وأن يثبت له من الأوصاف ما منفي عن ضده، والعكس بالعكس من غير ما حاجة إلى طلب الأوصاف التي تعرف بها مطابقته لذاته. من ذلك ما أورده الطوفي في شرحه على مختصره لروضة الناظر لابن قدامة : قوله : (المكروه ضد المندوب)، قلت: يظهر تضادهما على ما مضى في المندوب، وذكر هنا .. وقد ظهر من تقسيم الخطاب إلى الأحكام أن المندوب : المأمور غير الجازم، والمكروه المنهي غير الجازم، فالمندوب قسيم الواجب في الأمر، والمكروه قسيم الحرام في النهي، فتحققت الضدية بينهما من حيث الحقيقة والمادة أي من حيث حقيقتهما ومادتهما. ومن ذلك أيضًا ما عرف به اللامشي الحنفي مصطلح الجهل، حيث قال : والجهل نقيض العلم ، وقيل : هو اعتقاد الشيء على خلاف ما هو به . والصحيح هو الأول.
Second: Definition by opposite or by opposition: its meaning is that one contrasts the defined term with its opposite, and establishes for it attributes that are negated from its opposite, and vice versa, without needing to seek the attributes by which its correspondence to its essence is known. Among that is what al-Tufi mentioned in his commentary on his abridgment of Rawdat al-Nazir by Ibn Qudama: his statement: 'The disliked (makruh) is the opposite of the recommended (mandub).' I say: their opposition appears based on what preceded regarding the mandub, and he mentioned here... And it has become clear from the division of address into rulings that the mandub is the commanded without decisiveness (ghayr jazim), and the makruh is the prohibited without decisiveness. So the mandub is the counterpart of the obligatory (wajib) in command, and the makruh is the counterpart of the forbidden (haram) in prohibition. Thus opposition is realized between them in terms of reality and matter, i.e., in terms of their reality and matter. And from that also is what al-Lamishi al-Hanafi defined as the term ignorance (jahl), where he said: 'Ignorance is the opposite (naqid) of knowledge, and it is said: it is belief in a thing contrary to what it is. And the correct is the first.'
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage explains the method of definition by opposite (al-ta'rif bi al-didd). The author begins by stating the principle: one contrasts the defined term with its opposite, assigning to the defined term attributes that are negated from the opposite, and vice versa, without needing to search for attributes that directly match the essence. Then he gives two examples. The first is from al-Tufi, who says 'the makruh (disliked) is the opposite of the mandub (recommended).' The author clarifies that this opposition is understood from the division of divine address into rulings: mandub is a command without decisiveness, makruh is a prohibition without decisiveness. Thus they are opposites in reality and matter. The second example is from al-Lamishi al-Hanafi defining 'jahl' (ignorance) as the opposite (naqid) of 'ilm (knowledge). He mentions an alternative definition (belief contrary to reality) but affirms the first as correct. Through these examples, the author illustrates how definition by opposite works in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
الضد (al-didd): The opposite; in this context, a method of definition where a term is defined by contrasting it with its clear opposite. [Note: In logic, 'didd' usually means 'contrary' (e.g., black vs. white); here it is used more broadly for opposition in legal rulings.]
المندوب (al-mandub): The recommended act; defined as that which is commanded without decisiveness (ghayr jazim).
المكروه (al-makruh): The disliked act; defined as that which is prohibited without decisiveness (ghayr jazim).
الجهل (al-jahl): Ignorance; defined as the opposite (naqid) of knowledge, i.e., absence of knowledge. [Note: In some texts, 'jahl' can mean ignorance as lack of knowledge; in others, it may mean false belief. The text prefers the opposite definition.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are identical in ruling.
B) They are opposites in the sense that one is commanded without decisiveness and the other is prohibited without decisiveness.
C) They are both types of wajib.
D) They are defined by their opposite 'ilm.

Key Takeaway
Definition by opposite is a valid and efficient method in jadal and usul al-fiqh, where a term is defined by contrasting it with its clear opposite.

?

Definition by Example in Jadal
Author explains definition by example with al-Baydawi's illustration of istiqra'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify definition by example and evaluate its completeness by noting missing essential attributes.

Core Idea
An example can illustrate, but it cannot replace a proper definition's essential attributes.

In this lesson, we examine the method of definition by example as used by al-Baydawi in defining istiqra' (induction). Although providing an example can clarify meaning, the author points out that it fails to convey the necessary and sufficient conditions. We will learn to recognize this method and assess its limitations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Locate the term 'istiqra'' in the passage. Al-Baydawi attempts to define it using an example.
The term is explicitly mentioned.
2
Extract the example given
Al-Baydawi's example: the witr prayer is performed on a mount, so it is not obligatory, due to induction of the obligatory acts. This is the illustration for istiqra'.
The example is indirect; it shows a result of induction rather than the process itself.
3
Determine the definition type
The author calls this 'definition by example'. It is not a formal definition (hadd) or description (rasm) but relies solely on an instance.
Definition by example is common in jadal contexts to quickly convey meaning.
4
Evaluate the definition's completeness
The author critiques that the example lacks essential attributes of istiqra'. Even the example is indirect—the actual induction is of legislative texts, not the witr prayer itself.
An example can insufficiently capture the essence of a term.
5
Understand why it matters in jadal
In dialectical settings, definitions must be precise to avoid ambiguity. An example may clarify but cannot substitute for a rigorous definition, which is necessary for valid argumentation.
This aligns with the broader principle that definitions must include genus and differentia.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثالثا : التعريف بالمثال : ومعناه أن يكتفى في تعريف المصطلح بإيراد مثال له يبين معناه، دون الحاجة إلى إيراد حد خاص به، من ذلك ما عرف به البيضاوي مصطلح الاستقراء، حيث قال : «الاستقراء، مثاله الوتر يؤدى على الراحلة، فلا يكون واجبا، لاستقراء الواجب» . فقد عرف البيضاوي الاستقراء بمثال له، ولم يبين صفاته اللازمة له التي يتميز بها عن غيره، وحتى المثال الذي ضربه لم يكن مثالاً مباشرًا وإنما كان مثالاً غير مباشر، فاستقراء أساليب الإيجاب في الألفاظ الشرعية هو الذي أفضى إلى إدراك أن الوتر ليس بواجب لأنه لم يثبت طلبه بهذه الأساليب.
Third: Definition by example: its meaning is that one suffices in defining a term by presenting an example that illustrates its meaning, without needing to provide a specific definition. Among that is what al-Baydawi defined as the term 'induction' (istiqra'), where he said: 'Induction: its example is that the witr prayer is performed on a mount, so it is not obligatory, due to induction of the obligatory (acts).' So al-Baydawi defined induction by an example for it, and he did not explain its essential attributes by which it is distinguished from others. Even the example he gave was not a direct example but an indirect example: for the induction of the methods of affirmation (al-ijab) in the legislative expressions is what led to the realization that witr is not obligatory because its demand was not established by these methods.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage discusses the method of definition by example (al-ta'rif bi al-mithal). The author explains that this method defines a term solely by providing an example that clarifies its meaning, without a formal definition. He gives the case of al-Baydawi defining 'istiqra'' (induction). Al-Baydawi said: 'Induction: its example is that the witr prayer is performed on a mount, so it is not obligatory, due to induction of the obligatory.' The author then critiques this definition, noting that al-Baydawi did not provide the essential attributes of induction, and that the example itself is indirect. The actual induction is of the methods of affirmation in legislative texts, which leads to the conclusion that witr is not obligatory because its demand is not established through those methods. Thus the example illustrates induction but does not directly define it.

Key Terms
الاستقراء
المثال
الوتر

Key Takeaway
Definition by example can illustrate but does not replace a proper definition; the example must clearly manifest the essence of the defined term.

Definition by Division in Jadal
Author explains definition by division with al-Razi's classification of knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct al-Razi's division of knowledge and explain how it functions as a definition by division.

Core Idea
Definition by division clarifies meaning by systematically classifying possibilities until only the defined term remains.

In jadal (dialectical debate), definitions are not always given as concise statements. Sometimes, the clearest way to define a term is to survey all the possibilities and isolate the intended meaning. This is called definition by division. In this lesson, we examine how Fakhr al-Din al-Razi uses this method to define knowledge and opinion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the starting point
Al-Razi begins with the mind's judgment (hukm al-dhihn) about something concerning something. This is the broad category being divided.
2
Follow the first division
He divides judgment into decisive (jazim) and non-decisive. Non-decisive falls under zann (opinion). Decisive moves to further divisions.
3
Trace the decisive branch
Decisive judgment is subdivided: it either corresponds (mutabiq) to reality or not. The corresponding branch leads to knowledge ('ilm). Then it further divides by cause: with cause (li-mujib) or without cause (badihiyyat?).
The 'no cause' branch leads to simple primary knowledge; the 'with cause' branch further subdivides.
4
Identify types of 'ilm by cause
Causes are sensory, intellectual, or composite. Sensory gives knowledge from senses and inner experiences. Intellectual is either mere conceptualization (badihiyyat) or requires other propositions (nazariyyat). Composite involves both sense and intellect (e.g., sam' - hearing).
5
Locate 'ilm and zann
'Ilm is found in the decisive, corresponding, with-cause branch (or without cause). Zann is the non-decisive judgment. The division exhausts all perceptions and clarifies the terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعا : التعريف بالتقسيم : ومقتضاه أن يقوم المعرف بسبر عناصر جملة معينة حتى يصل إلى العنصر المراد تعريفه من بين عناصرها، فيتضح معناه في الذهن دون أن يحتاج إلى ضبطه في عبارة محددة . ومثاله، ما نجده عند الإمام فخر الدين الرازي في تعريفه لمصطلحي العلم والظن فهو لم يحدهما بعبارة موجزة كما هو حال كل تعريف أو حد، وإنما سبر وقسم كل مراتب الإدراك حتى اتضح من بينها معنى كل من العلم والظن . . قال : إن حكم الذهن بأمر على أمر إما أن يكون جازما أو لا يكون. فإن كان جازما : فإما أن يكون مطابقا للمحكوم عليه أو لا يكون . فإن كان مطابقا فإما أن يكون لموجب أو لا يكون. فإن كان لموجب : فالموجب إما أن يكون حسيّا»، أو «عقليّا» أو «مركبًا منهما، فإن كان «حسيّا»، فهو العلم الحاصل من الحواس الخمسة، ويقرب منه العلم بالأمور الوجدانية كاللذة والألم. وإن كان «عقليّا»، فإما أن يكون الموجب مجرد تصور طرفي القضية، أو لابد من شيء آخر من القضايا، فالأول هو «البدهيات»، والثاني «النظريات». وأما إن كان الموجب مركبًا من الحس والعقل فإما أن يكون من السمع
Fourth: Definition by division: its requirement is that the definer surveys the elements of a certain set until he reaches the element intended to be defined among its elements, so its meaning becomes clear in the mind without needing to fix it in a specific expression. An example is what we find with Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi in his definition of the terms knowledge ('ilm) and opinion (zann): he did not define them with a concise expression as is the case with every definition or limit, but rather surveyed and divided all the ranks of perception until the meaning of each of knowledge and opinion became clear among them. He said: 'The mind's judgment about something concerning something is either decisive or not. If it is decisive, then it either corresponds to the thing judged or not. If it corresponds, then it is either due to a cause or not. If due to a cause, then the cause is either sensory, intellectual, or composed of both. If it is sensory, then it is knowledge obtained from the five senses, and close to it is knowledge of matters of inner experience (wijdaniyyat) such as pleasure and pain. If it is intellectual, then the cause is either a mere conceptualization (tasawwur) of the two terms of the proposition, or it necessitates something else from among propositions. The first is 'primary beliefs' (badihiyyat), the second is 'theoretical beliefs' (nazariyyat). As for the cause composed of sense and intellect, it is either from hearing (sam')...'
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage explains the method of definition by division (al-ta'rif bi al-taqsim). The author describes that the definer surveys the elements of a set until he reaches the intended element, thereby clarifying its meaning without a fixed expression. He then presents an example from Fakhr al-Din al-Razi's definition of 'ilm (knowledge) and zann (opinion). Al-Razi did not use a concise definition but instead divided all ranks of perception. He began by distinguishing decisive judgment from non-decisive. If decisive, it may correspond to reality or not. If it corresponds, it may be due to a cause or not. If due to a cause, that cause is sensory, intellectual, or composite. Sensory cause gives knowledge from the five senses and inner experiences. Intellectual cause is either mere conceptualization of the proposition's terms (giving primary beliefs) or requires other propositions (giving theoretical beliefs). Composite cause is from hearing (sam') — which continues beyond the passage. Through this division, al-Razi defines knowledge and opinion by their placement in the hierarchy.

Key Terms
العلم
الظن
البدهيات
النظريات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In al-Razi's classification, what distinguishes badihiyyat from nazariyyat?

B) Badihiyyat arise from mere conceptualization of the proposition's terms, while nazariyyat require other propositions.
C) Badihiyyat are composite of sense and intellect.
D) Badihiyyat are non-decisive judgments.

Key Takeaway
Definition by division clarifies meaning by exhausting possibilities through binary divisions, leaving only the intended term.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
